Eating Before Eid al-Fitr Prayer: A Recommended Practice
Ruling with proofs from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating before Eid al-Fitr prayer and identify the proofs that support it.

Core Idea
Eating before Eid al-Fitr is recommended, not obligatory, based on the Prophet's practice.

The source text opens a new section on the two Eid prayers and immediately addresses a specific Sunnah: eating before leaving for the Eid al-Fitr prayer. This practice is deeply rooted in the Prophet's example and is emphasized by the Hanafi school as a recommended act (mustahabb). In this lesson, we will examine the ruling and the evidence from both the Quran and the Sunnah that supports it.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the explicit statement in the text: 'yustahabb' (it is recommended). Note that the Hanafi school classifies this as mustahabb (sunnah muakkadah), not wajib.
The ruling applies specifically to Eid al-Fitr, not to Eid al-Adha.
2
Examine the Quranic proofs
The author cites two verses: one commanding to complete the fast and glorify Allah (2:185) and another commanding prayer and sacrifice (108:2). Understand how these verses are used to support the recommendation of eating before the prayer.
The verses are cited as wajh (proof) for the ruling, though the connection is indirect.
3
Analyze the hadith proofs
The text provides multiple hadith, especially the one from Anas that the Prophet would eat dates before going out. Note the detail that he ate them in odd numbers.
The hadith show consistent practice (fi'l), which in Hanafi usul indicates recommendation, not obligation.
4
Understand juridical reasoning
Apply Hanafi usul: the Prophet's continuous practice without an explicit command yields istihbab (recommendation). Recognize that the absence of a command makes it mustahabb rather than wajib.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from any claim of obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْعِيدَيْنِ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ أَنْ يَطْعَمَ الْإِنْسَانُ قَبْلَ الْخُرُوجِ إِلَى الْمُصَلَّىٰ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلِتُكْمِلُوا الْعِدَّةَ وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا اللَّهَ عَلَىٰ مَا هَدَاكُمْ وَلَعَلَّكُمْ تَشْكُرُونَ (سورة البقرة ٢، آية ١٨٥) وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَانْحَرْ (سورة الكوثر ١٠٨، آية ٢) وَجْهٌ: (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَخْرُجُ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ وَالْأَضْحَىٰ إِلَى الْمُصَلَّىٰ، فَأَوَّلُ شَيْءٍ يَبْدَأُ بِهِ الصَّلَاةُ، ثُمَّ يَنْصَرِفُ، فَيَقُومُ مُقَابِلَ النَّاسِ، وَالنَّاسُ جُلُوسٌ عَلَىٰ صُفُوفِهِمْ، فَيَعِظُهُمْ وَيُوصِيهِمْ وَيَأْمُرُهُمْ (بخاري شريف: باب الخروج إلى المصلى بغير منبر، نمبر ٩٥٦) وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ عَنْ أَنَسٍ قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا يَغْدُو يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ حَتَّىٰ يَأْكُلَ تَمَرَاتٍ. وَقَالَ مُرَجَّأُ بْنُ رَجَاءٍ: حَدَّثَنِي عُبَيْدُ اللَّهِ قَالَ: حَدَّثَنِي أَنَسٌ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: وَيَأْكُلُهُنَّ وِتْرًا (بخاري شريف: باب الأكل يوم الفطر قبل الخروج نمبر ٩٥٣، ترمذي شريف: باب في الأكل يوم الفطر قبل الخروج، نمبر ٥٤٢) وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا يَخْرُجُ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ حَتَّىٰ يَطْعَمَ، وَلَا يَأْكُلُ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ حَتَّىٰ يَذْبَحَ (سنن بيهقي: باب يترك الأكل يوم النحر حتى يرجع نمبر ٦١٥٩، ترمذي شريف: باب في الأكل يوم الفطر قبل الخروج، نمبر ٥٤٢) وَجْهٌ: (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، قَالَ: كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا يَخْرُجُ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ حَتَّىٰ يَطْعَمَ، وَلَا يَطْعَمُ يَوْمَ الْأَضْحَىٰ حَتَّىٰ يُصَلِّيَ (ترمذي شريف: باب في الأكل يوم الفطر قبل الخروج، نمبر ٥٤٢، سنن ابن ماجه: باب الأكل يوم الفطر قبل أن يخرج، نمبر ١٧٥٦)
Chapter on the prayer of the two Eids. It is recommended on the day of Fitr that a person eat before going out to the musalla. Proof (1): The verse: '...that you complete the number and magnify Allah...' (Quran 2:185). Proof (2): The verse: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' (Quran 108:2). Proof (3): The hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would go out on Fitr and Adha to the musalla, and the first thing he would begin with was the prayer, then he would turn and stand facing the people while they sat in their rows, and he would admonish them and command them. Proof (1): The hadith from Anas who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten some dates... and he would eat them odd in number. Proof (2): The hadith from Abdullah ibn Buraidah from his father who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten, and he would not eat on the day of Nahr until he had sacrificed. Proof (3): The hadith from Abdullah ibn Buraidah from his father who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten, and he would not eat on the day of Adha until he had prayed.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs establishing the recommendation (istihbab) of eating before the Eid al-Fitr prayer. The author begins by stating the ruling: it is mustahabb (recommended) to eat before going to the musalla (prayer ground). Then he provides multiple proofs. The first two are Quranic verses: the command to complete the fast and glorify Allah (2:185) and the command to pray and sacrifice (108:2). These are cited to support the idea of eating before the prayer, as eating is a form of completing the fast and showing gratitude. Then he gives several hadiths. The first shows the Prophet's practice of beginning with the prayer on Eid. The second from Anas specifies that he would eat dates before going out, and he would eat them in odd numbers. The third and fourth from Abdullah ibn Buraidah emphasize that he would not go out on Fitr without eating, whereas on Adha he would not eat until after the prayer or after sacrificing. Collectively, these narrations establish the recommended nature of eating on Fitr before the prayer.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended act that brings reward but no punishment for omission.
عيد الفطر (Eid al-Fitr): The festival marking the end of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on eating before the Eid al-Fitr prayer?
A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Haram (prohibited)
D) Mubah (permissible but not rewarding)

Key Takeaway
Eating before Eid al-Fitr prayer is a confirmed sunnah (mustahabb) in the Hanafi school, supported by the Prophet's practice and Islamic legal reasoning.

Obligation of Eid Prayer and Its Conditions
Concise statement linking Eid prayer obligation to Jumu'ah conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Eid prayer is wajib and identify the conditions that must be met for its obligation.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib on those same people who are obligated for Jumu'ah.

This short but powerful statement from al-Quduri’s matn establishes a clear link between the Eid prayer and the Friday prayer. In the Hanafi school, the obligation of Eid prayer is not absolute; rather, it is contingent on the same conditions that make Jumu'ah obligatory. This lesson unpacks that link and clarifies who must perform the Eid prayer and on what basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that Eid prayer is wājib. Understand that in Hanafi terminology, wājib is a binding obligation established by zannī (non-definitive) evidence, distinct from farḍ which comes from qaṭʿī evidence.
Memorize: wājib = obligatory but from zannī dalīl.
2
Identify the condition for obligation
The obligation applies to the same person who is obligated to perform Jumu'ah. Therefore, you must recall the conditions for Jumu'ah: being Muslim, adult, sane, free, male, resident (muqim), healthy, and not blind.
Jumu'ah is farḍ ʿayn only on those meeting these conditions.
3
Apply the conditions to Eid
Since Eid shares the same conditions, the Eid prayer is wājib only on those who are free, male, resident, healthy, and not blind. Women, travelers, the sick, and the blind are not obligated.
This is a key point of difference from other schools.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilāf
Imam al-Shāfiʿī considers Eid prayer to be sunnah muʾakkadah, not wājib. Understand the thamarah al-khilāf: for Hanafis, leaving it without excuse is sinful; for Shāfiʿīs, it is merely abandoning a recommended act.
Know the practical consequence of the disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول: عید کی نماز ہر اس شخص پر واجب ہے جس پر جمعہ ہے، عید کی وہی شرائط ہیں جو جمعہ کے شرائط ہیں۔
Principle: The Eid prayer is obligatory on every person upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory, and the Eid prayer has the same conditions as the Jumu'ah prayer.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This is a terse ruling from the matn establishing that the Eid prayer (both Fitr and Adha) carries the same level of obligation and conditions as the Jumu'ah (Friday) prayer. In the Hanafi school, Jumu'ah is a fard 'ayn for free, adult, male, resident Muslims who are not blind or sick. Thus, Eid prayer is also wajib (necessary/obligatory) on the same category of people. The conditions include: being a resident (muqim), male, free, healthy, and not blind. Women, travelers, and those who are ill or blind are not obligated. This ruling is based on analogy between Eid and Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligation that is less than fard, established by zanni evidence.
شرائط (shurut): Conditions for obligation and validity, such as residence, masculinity, freedom, health, etc.
جمعہ (jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer, farḍ ʿayn on those who meet its conditions.
عید (eid): The two annual festivals: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, on whom is the Eid prayer obligatory?
A) All Muslims, men and women
B) Only men
C) Those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory
D) All residents, including women

Key Takeaway
The Eid prayer is wājib in the Hanafi school, and its obligation applies only to those who meet the same conditions as for Jumu'ah: free, male, resident, healthy, and not blind.

Recommended Acts for Eid: Ghusl, Perfume, and Takbir Dispute
Rulings and intra-Hanafi dispute on takbir during the walk to musalla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi positions on takbir while walking to the Eid musalla and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds that one does not say takbir on the way to the Eid musalla; the Sahibayn hold that one does.

This lesson covers the recommended acts (sunan) for the day of Eid, including ghusl and perfume. It then delves into an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding saying takbir on the way to the musalla. This dispute illustrates how the Hanafi school sometimes has differing opinions between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main students, and which position is ultimately relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
The passage lists several sunan for Eid: ghusl, perfume, walking to the musalla, miswak, eating sweet, takbir al-tashriq, good clothes, sadaqat al-fitr.
2
State the takbir dispute
The text explicitly states that according to Abu Hanifa, one does not say takbir on the way, while according to the Sahibayn, one does.
The terms 'indahuma' refer to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Analyze the evidence for each
For Abu Hanifa: the saying of Shu'bah that Ibn Abbas disapproved of people saying takbir before the imam. For Sahibayn: hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet said takbir from his house to the musalla, and the practice of Ibn Umar.
4
Understand the tarjih
The matn presents Abu Hanifa's view first and it is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. The Sahibayn's view is acknowledged but not adopted for fatwa.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the evidence according to Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
A Hanafi should not say takbir on the way to the musalla. One may walk silently or engage in dhikr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وَمُحَمَّدٍ) وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَغْتَسِلَ وَيَتَطَيَّبَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَغْتَسِلُ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ وَيَوْمَ الْأَضْحَىٰ (سُنَنُ ابْنِ مَاجَه: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْاغْتِسَالِ فِي الْعِيدَيْنِ، نَمْبَر ١٣١٥) وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَغْتَسِلَ وَيَتَطَيَّبَ عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ وَأَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَا: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: مَنِ اغْتَسَلَ يَوْمَ الْجُمُعَةِ، وَلَبِسَ مِنْ أَحْسَنِ ثِيَابِهِ، وَمَسَّ مِنْ طِيبٍ إِنْ كَانَ عِنْدَهُ، ثُمَّ أَتَى الْجُمُعَةَ (سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ شَرِيف: بَابُ فِي الْغُسْلِ لِلْجُمُعَةِ، نَمْبَر ٣٤٣) وَجْهٌ: (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَغْتَسِلَ وَيَتَطَيَّبَ أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عُمَرَ قَالَ: أَخَذَ عُمَرُ جُبَّةً مِنْ إِسْتَبْرَقٍ تُبَاعُ فِي السُّوقِ، فَأَخَذَهَا فَأَتَى رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، ابْتَعْ هَذِهِ تَجَمَّلْ لِلْعِيدِ وَالْوُفُودِ (بُخَارِي شَرِيف: بَابُ فِي الْعِيدَيْنِ وَالتَّجَمُّلِ فِيهِ، نَمْبَر ٩٤٨) وَجْهٌ: (١) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَتَوَجَّهَ إِلَى الْمُصَلَّىٰ وَلَا يُكَبِّرُ فِي طَرِيقِ الْمُصَلَّىٰ عَنْ شُعْبَةَ، قَالَ: كُنْتُ أَقُودُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ، يَوْمَ الْعِيدِ، فَيَسْمَعُ النَّاسَ يُكَبِّرُونَ، فَقَالَ: مَا شَأْنُ النَّاسِ؟ قُلْتُ: يُكَبِّرُونَ، قَالَ: يُكَبِّرُونَ؟ قَالَ: يُكَبِّرُ الْإِمَامُ؟ قُلْتُ: لَا، قَالَ: أَجَانِينُ النَّاسُ (مُصَنَّفُ ابْنِ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ فِي التَّكْبِيرِ إِذَا خَرَجَ إِلَى الْعِيدِ، نَمْبَر ٥٦٣٠) وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَتَوَجَّهَ إِلَى الْمُصَلَّىٰ وَلَا يُكَبِّرُ فِي طَرِيقِ الْمُصَلَّىٰ أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عُمَرَ أَخْبَرَهُ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يُكَبِّرُ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ مِنْ حِينِ يَخْرُجُ مِنْ بَيْتِهِ حَتَّىٰ يَأْتِيَ الْمُصَلَّىٰ (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ: كِتَابُ الْعِيدَيْنِ، نَمْبَر ١٧١٤، مُسْتَدْرَكُ الْحَاكِمِ: كِتَابُ صَلَاةِ الْعِيدَيْنِ، نَمْبَر ١١٠٥) وَجْهٌ: (٣) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَتَوَجَّهَ إِلَى الْمُصَلَّىٰ وَلَا يُكَبِّرُ فِي طَرِيقِ الْمُصَلَّىٰ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّهُ كَانَ إِذَا غَدَا يَوْمَ الْأَضْحَىٰ وَيَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ يَجْهَرُ بِالتَّكْبِيرِ حَتَّىٰ يَأْتِيَ الْمُصَلَّىٰ، ثُمَّ يُكَبِّرُ حَتَّىٰ يَأْتِيَ الْإِمَامُ (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ: كِتَابُ الْعِيدَيْنِ، نَمْبَر ١٧١٦) أُصُولٌ: عِيدُ الْفِطْرِ كَثِيرٌ مِنَ السُّنَنِ: ١- مِسْوَاكٌ ٢- غُسْلٌ ٣- أَكْلُ شَيْءٍ حُلْوٍ قَبْلَ الْخُرُوجِ ٤- تَكْبِيرُ التَّشْرِيقِ ٥- طِيبٌ ٦- ثِيَابٌ حَسَنَةٌ ٧- صَدَقَةُ الْفِطْرِ
And it is recommended that he bathe and apply perfume and proceed to the musalla, and he does not say takbir on the way to the musalla according to Abu Hanifa, and he says takbir on the way to the musalla according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Proof (1): The hadith for bathing and perfuming: from Ibn Abbas... Proof (2): The hadith for bathing and perfuming: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Abu Hurairah... Proof (3): The hadith for bathing and perfuming: that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar said... Proof (1): The saying of the Tabi'i for proceeding to the musalla and not saying takbir: from Shu'bah... Proof (2): The hadith for proceeding to the musalla and not saying takbir: that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar informed him... Proof (3): The saying of the Sahabi for proceeding to the musalla and not saying takbir: from Ibn 'Umar... Principles: Many sunan of Eid al-Fitr: 1. Miswak, 2. Ghusl, 3. Eating something sweet before going out, 4. Takbir al-Tashriq, 5. Perfume, 6. Good clothes, 7. Sadaqat al-Fitr.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage covers several recommended acts (sunan) for the day of Eid, along with an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding takbir on the way to the musalla. The text first lists: performing ghusl (bath), applying perfume, and walking to the musalla. Then it addresses takbir: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, one should not say takbir on the way to the musalla; according to his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, one should say takbir. The proofs provided for the recommended acts include hadith from Ibn Abbas, Abu Sa'id, and Ibn Umar showing that the Prophet bathed on Eid, wore good clothes, and used perfume. For the takbir dispute, the text gives a saying of the Tabi'i (Shu'bah) narrating that Ibn Abbas criticized people who were saying takbir before the imam began, implying it is not recommended to say takbir individually. Then there is a hadith from Ibn Umar stating that the Prophet would say takbir from his house until the musalla. The third proof is a saying of the Sahabi (Ibn Umar) that he used to say takbir loudly. The author then provides a summary of seven sunan of Eid al-Fitr: miswak, ghusl, eating something sweet before going out, reciting takbir al-tashriq, applying perfume, wearing good clothes, and giving sadaqat al-fitr.

Key Terms
تکبیر تشریق (takbir al-tashriq): The phrase 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillah al-hamd' recited after each fard prayer from Fajr of the 9th of Dhul Hijjah until Asr of the 13th.
عند أبي حنيفة (inda Abi Hanifah): The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa.
عندهما (indahuma): The opinion of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what should one do regarding takbir on the way to the Eid musalla?
A) Say takbir loudly
B) Remain silent, not saying takbir
C) Recite Quran instead
D) Say takbir only if walking alone

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi position is that one should not say takbir on the way to the Eid musalla, following the view of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Eid Prayer: Wajib Status, Timing, Takbirs, and Khutbah
Core rulings of Eid prayer: time, takbirs, recitation, and khutbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer (wajib), identify its time (from sunrise to zenith), describe the prescribed number of rak'ahs and extra takbirs (six total, three per rak'ah), and explain why no nafl is performed before it in the musalla.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib: two rak'ahs with six extra takbirs, no nafl before it in the musalla, and the khutbah after the prayer.

Eid prayer is a distinctive congregational worship performed twice a year. The Hanafi school, drawing on the practice of the Prophet and the Caliphs, classifies it as wajib – a level between fard and sunnah. This lesson unpacks the key rulings from al-Quduri's matn: the time window, the structure of the prayer, the extra takbirs, and the post-prayer sermon. By understanding these elements, you will grasp how the Hanafi school systematizes an act of worship that is both festive and legally structured.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text begins with 'باب صلاة العيدين' – the chapter on the prayer of the two Eids. The Hanafi ruling is that this prayer is wajib (necessary). Recognise that this is a higher level than sunnah but lower than fard, based on the consistent practice of the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs.
Wajib here means it is obligatory to perform, but its evidence is zanni in transmission (ahad hadith).
2
Determine the time of Eid prayer
The text says: 'فَإِذَا حَلَّتْ الصَّلَاةُ بِارْتِفَاعِ الشَّمْسِ دَخَلَ وَقْتُهَا إِلَى الزَّوَالِ' – the time begins when the sun has risen (about 15-20 minutes after sunrise) and ends at zenith. This is a condition (shart) for the prayer's validity.
The time is derived from the practice of the Companions and is consistent across the schools.
3
Analyse the structure of the prayer
The imam leads two rak'ahs. In the first rak'ah: takbirat al-ihram, then three extra takbirs, then recitation (Fatihah + surah), then takbir for ruku. In the second rak'ah: after recitation (Fatihah + surah), three extra takbirs, then takbir for ruku. This gives six extra takbirs total. The hands are raised with each takbir, and recitation is aloud.
The Urdu usul confirms the six extra takbirs: three before qira'ah in the first rak'ah and three after qira'ah before ruku in the second.
4
Note the prohibition of nafl before Eid prayer
The text explicitly states: 'وَلَا يُنْتَفَلُ فِي الْمُصَلَّى قَبْلَ صَلَاةِ الْعِيدِ' – no supererogatory prayer is performed in the musalla before the Eid prayer. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet did not pray any nafl before or after the Eid prayer in the prayer ground.
This ruling is specific to the musalla; nafl can be prayed at home before or after.
5
Understand the khutbah after the prayer
The imam delivers two sermons (khutbah) after the prayer, teaching the people about sadaqat al-fitr (the charity of breaking the fast) and its rulings. This differs from Jumu'ah where the khutbah precedes the prayer.
The khutbah after Eid prayer is a distinctive Hanafi ruling; other schools may place it before.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْعِيدَيْنِ وَلَا يُنْتَفَلُ فِي الْمُصَلَّى قَبْلَ صَلَاةِ الْعِيدِ فَإِذَا حَلَّتْ الصَّلَاةُ بِارْتِفَاعِ الشَّمْسِ دَخَلَ وَقْتُهَا إِلَى الزَّوَالِ وَيُصَلِّي الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ يُكَبِّرُ فِي الْأُولَى تَكْبِيرَةَ الْإِحْرَامِ وَثَلَاثًا بَعْدَهَا ثُمَّ يَقْرَأُ فَاتِحَةَ الْكِتَابِ وَسُورَةً مَعَهَا وَيُكَبِّرُ تَكْبِيرَةً يَرْكَعُ بِهَا ثُمَّ يَقُومُ فِي الثَّانِيَةِ فَيَقْرَأُ فَاتِحَةَ الْكِتَابِ وَسُورَةً وَيُكَبِّرُ ثَلَاثًا وَيَرْكَعُ بِتَكْبِيرَةٍ وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ فِي تَكْبِيرَاتِ الْعِيدَيْنِ وَيَجْهَرُ بِالْقِرَاءَةِ فِي صَلَاةِ الْعِيدَيْنِ ثُمَّ يَخْطُبُ بَعْدَ الصَّلَاةِ خُطْبَتَيْنِ يُعَلِّمُ النَّاسَ فِيهَا صَدَقَةَ الْفِطْرِ وَأَحْكَامَهَا أصول: عیدین کی نماز میں چھ زائد تکبیریں ہیں اس طرح کہ پہلی رکعت میں قرائت سے پہلے تین تکبیریں اور دوسری رکعت میں قرائت کے بعد رکوع سے پہلے تین تکبیریں، ان تکبیرات میں رفع یدین بھی کرے۔
Chapter of the prayer of the two Eids. And no supererogatory prayer is performed in the musalla before the Eid prayer. When the prayer becomes permissible by the rising of the sun, its time enters until the zenith. And the imam leads the people in two rak'ahs. He says takbirat al-ihram in the first (rak'ah) and three after it, then he recites the Opening of the Book and a surah with it, and he says a takbir by which he bows. Then he stands for the second (rak'ah), recites the Opening of the Book and a surah, and says three takbirs, and bows with a takbir. And he raises his hands in the takbirs of the two Eids. And he recites aloud in the prayer of the two Eids. Then he delivers two sermons after the prayer, teaching the people therein the charity of breaking the fast and its rulings. Principle: In the prayer of the two Eids, there are six extra takbirs: in the first rak'ah, three takbirs before recitation; in the second rak'ah, three takbirs after recitation but before bowing. Raising the hands is also done in these takbirs.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri presents the chapter on the Eid prayer. It is a ruling statement with supporting hadith (not fully quoted here). The text begins by stating that no supererogatory prayer (nafl) is performed in the musalla (the prayer ground) before the Eid prayer. This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported by Ibn Abbas. The time for Eid prayer begins when the sun has risen to the height of a spear (approximately 15-20 minutes after sunrise) and continues until the sun reaches its zenith (zawal). This is derived from reports of the Companions. The imam leads the congregation in two rak'ahs. In the first rak'ah, he says the takbirat al-ihram (the opening takbir), then three additional takbirs, after which he recites Surah al-Fatihah and another surah. Then he says a takbir to go into ruku'. In the second rak'ah, after reciting al-Fatihah and a surah, he says three takbirs before going into ruku' with a takbir. He raises his hands with each takbir of the Eid prayer. The recitation is done aloud. After the prayer, the imam delivers two khutbahs (sermons) in which he teaches the people about sadaqat al-fitr and its rulings. The Urdu usul note clarifies that there are six extra takbirs total: three before recitation in the first rak'ah and three after recitation but before ruku' in the second rak'ah, and the hands are raised with these takbirs. This is the Hanafi position, based on the practice of the Companions.

Key Terms
صلاة العيدين (Ṣalāt al-‘Īdayn): The special congregational prayer performed on the two Islamic festivals: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.
تكبير (Takbīr): The utterance of 'Allāhu Akbar' at specific points in the Eid prayer, including extra takbirs beyond the standard ones.
مصلى (Muṣallā): The open prayer ground outside the mosque where Eid prayer is typically performed.
خطبة (Khutbah): The sermon delivered after the Eid prayer, consisting of two parts with a short sitting in between.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many extra takbirs are there in the Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Four extra takbirs total
B) Six extra takbirs total (three in each rak'ah)
C) Seven in the first rak'ah and five in the second
D) No extra takbirs

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school, performed in two rak'ahs with six extra takbirs, no nafl before it in the musalla, and the khutbah after the prayer teaches about Zakat al-Fitr.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Eid Prayer: Takbirs, Recitation, and Sermon
Ruling on the number of takbirs, raising hands, jahr, and sermon for Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi modal practice for Eid prayer (takbirs, jahr, sermon after prayer) and explain the evidence and differ with Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Eid prayer has extra takbirs, jahr, and post-prayer sermon—all sunnah mu'akkadah, supported by Companion practice.

The Eid prayer is a communal celebration with distinctive features: additional takbirs, audible recitation, and a sermon after the prayer. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position from the matn of al-Quduri, showing how each element is a sunnah mu'akkadah rooted in the practice of the Companions and confirmed by hadith. We will also examine the Shafi'i difference regarding the timing of the sermon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts prescribed
Read the matn carefully and list each element: opening takbir, extra takbirs, recitation, takbir for ruku', raising hands, jahr, sermon after prayer.
The matn gives a step-by-step description of the imam's actions.
2
Classify the ruling level
Determine the hukm for each element. The Eid prayer itself is wajib (Abu Hanifa), but the specific practices described (extra takbirs, etc.) are sunnah mu'akkadah according to the Hanafi school.
Check the hanafi_position_box for details.
3
Analyze the first evidence (takbirs)
Examine the hadith of Abu Musa and Hudhayfah. Note that the four takbirs include the opening takbir, meaning three extra. Also consider the report of Ibn Mas'ud confirming the same.
The phrase 'صَدَقَ' confirms the practice.
4
Analyze the dispute on sermon timing
The matn states the sermon is after the prayer. The text then cites the Shafi'i evidence (Ibn 'Umar hadith) showing prayer before sermon. Compare: Hanafi say the known practice includes sermon after, but the hadith does not contradict because it only states that prayer precedes the sermon (which both agree on). The dispute is whether the sermon is before or after.
See madhhab_dispute_map for full analysis.
5
Confirm other sunan (raising hands, jahr)
Raising hands is established from 'Umar's practice (though chain is munqati') and jahr from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. These are sunnah mu'akkadah.
The evidence for raising hands is weaker but acceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْعِيدَيْنِ يُكَبِّرُ فِي الْأُولَى تَكْبِيرَةَ الْإِحْرَامِ وَثَلَاثًا بَعْدَهَا ثُمَّ يَقْرَأُ فَاتِحَةَ الْكِتَابِ وَسُورَةً مَعَهَا وَيُكَبِّرُ تَكْبِيرَةً يَرْكَعُ بِهَا وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ فِي تَكْبِيرَاتِ الْعِيدَيْنِ وَيَجْهَرُ بِالْقِرَاءَةِ فِي صَلَاةِ الْعِيدَيْنِ ثُمَّ يَخْطُبُ بَعْدَ الصَّلَاةِ خُطْبَتَيْنِ يُعَلِّمُ النَّاسَ فِيهَا صَدَقَةَ الْفِطْرِ وَأَحْكَامَهَا. وَجْهٌ: (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ يُكَبِّرُ فِي الْأُولَى تَكْبِيرَةَ الْإِحْرَامِ سَأَلَ أَبَا مُوسَى الْأَشْعَرِيَّ وَحُذَيْفَةَ بْنَ الْيَمَانِ، كَيْفَ كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ يُكَبِّرُ فِي الْأَضْحَى وَالْفِطْرِ؟ فَقَالَ أَبُو مُوسَى : كَانَ يُكَبِّرُ أَرْبَعًا تَكْبِيرَهُ عَلَى الْجَنَائِزِ، فَقَالَ حُذَيْفَةُ : صَدَقَ (سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ: بَابُ التَّكْبِيرِ فِي الْعِيدَيْنِ، رَقْم 1153 سُنَنُ الْبَيْهَقِيِّ: بَابُ ذِكْرِ الْخَبَرِ الَّذِي رُوِيَ فِي التَّكْبِيرِ أَرْبَعًا، رَقْم 6183) وَجْهٌ: (2) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ يُكَبِّرُ فِي الْأُولَى تَكْبِيرَةَ الْإِحْرَامِ فَأَسْنَدُوا أَمْرَهُمْ إِلَى ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ، فَقَالَ: تُكَبِّرُ أَرْبَعًا قَبْلَ الْقِرَاءَةِ ثُمَّ تَقْرَأُ، فَإِذَا فَرَغْتَ كَبَّرْتَ فَرَكَعْتَ ثُمَّ تَقُومُ فِي الثَّانِيَةِ فَتَقْرَأُ، فَإِذَا فَرَغْتَ كَبَّرْتَ أَرْبَعًا (سُنَنُ الْبَيْهَقِيِّ: بَابُ ذِكْرِ الْخَبَرِ الَّذِي رُوِيَ فِي التَّكْبِيرِ أَرْبَعًا، رَقْم 6183 مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ: بَابُ كَمْ بَيْنَ كُلِّ تَكْبِيرَتَيْنِ، رَقْم 5687) وَجْهٌ: (1) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ يُكَبِّرُ فِي الْأُولَى تَكْبِيرَةَ الْإِحْرَامِ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَبُو بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرُ رضي الله عنهما يُصَلُّونَ الْعِيدَيْنِ قَبْلَ الْخُطْبَةِ (بُخَارِيُّ شَرِيفٍ: بَابُ الْخُطْبَةِ بَعْدَ الْعِيدِ، رَقْم 963) وَجْهٌ: (1) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ فِي تَكْبِيرَاتِ الْعِيدَيْنِ أَنَّ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ كَانَ يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ مَعَ كُلِّ تَكْبِيرَةِ فِي الْجِنَازَةِ وَالْعِيدَيْنِ. وَهَذَا مُنْقَطِعٌ (سُنَنُ الْبَيْهَقِيِّ: بَابُ رَفْعِ الْيَدَيْنِ فِي تَكْبِيرِ الْعِيدِ رَقْم 6189 مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ: بَابُ التَّكْبِيرِ بِالْيَدَيْنِ، رَقْم 5699) وَجْهٌ: (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَجْهَرُ بِالْقِرَاءَةِ فِي صَلَاةِ الْعِيدَيْنِ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَبُو بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرُ رضي الله عنهما يُصَلُّونَ الْعِيدَيْنِ قَبْلَ الْخُطْبَةِ (بُخَارِيُّ شَرِيفٍ: بَابُ الْخُطْبَةِ بَعْدَ الْعِيدِ، رَقْم 963 مُسْلِمٌ شَرِيفٌ كِتَابُ صَلَاةِ الْعِيدَيْنِ، رَقْم 884) وَجْهٌ: (2) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَجْهَرُ بِالْقِرَاءَةِ فِي صَلَاةِ الْعِيدَيْنِ سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ:
Chapter of the Eid Prayer: He makes the opening takbir in the first (rak'ah) and three after it, then recites the Opening of the Book and a surah with it, and makes a takbir with which he bows, and he raises his hands during the takbirs of the two Eids, and he recites aloud in the Eid prayer, then he delivers a sermon after the prayer, two sermons, in which he teaches the people Zakat al-Fitr and its rules. Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing 'he makes the opening takbir in the first': He asked Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and Hudhayfah ibn al-Yaman: How would the Messenger of Allah make the takbir on Adha and Fitr? Abu Musa said: He would make four takbirs like his takbir over the funerals. Hudhayfah said: He spoke truth (Sunan Abi Dawud: Chapter of Takbir in the Eids, no. 1153; Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter citing the report narrated about four takbirs, no. 6183). Evidence (2): The saying of a Tabi'i for establishing 'he makes the opening takbir in the first': They attributed their matter to Ibn Mas'ud, and he said: You make four takbirs before the recitation, then recite, and when you finish, you make the takbir and bow, then stand in the second (rak'ah) and recite, and when you finish, you make four takbirs (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter citing the report narrated about four takbirs, no. 6183; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq: Chapter how many between each two takbirs, no. 5687). Evidence (1): The proof of al-Shafi'i: the hadith for establishing 'he makes the opening takbir in the first': From Ibn 'Umar who said: The Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, and 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, used to pray the two Eids before the sermon (Sahih al-Bukhari: Chapter of the sermon after the Eid, no. 963). Evidence (1): The saying of a Sahabi for establishing 'he raises his hands during the takbirs of the two Eids': That 'Umar ibn al-Khattab used to raise his hands with every takbir in the funeral prayer and the two Eids. This is disconnected (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter of raising the hands in the takbir of the Eid, no. 6189; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq: Chapter of the takbir with hands, no. 5699). Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing 'he recites aloud in the Eid prayer': From Ibn 'Umar who said: The Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, and 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, used to pray the two Eids before the sermon (Sahih al-Bukhari: Chapter of the sermon after the Eid, no. 963; Sahih Muslim: Book of the Eid prayer, no. 884). Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing 'he recites aloud in the Eid prayer': I heard Ibn 'Abbas saying: ...
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on Eid prayer. The matn states the Hanafi ruling: the imam begins the first rak'ah with the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram), then adds three extra takbirs, then recites al-Fatihah and a surah, then makes a takbir to go into ruku'. He raises his hands with each takbir, recites aloud, and delivers two sermons after the prayer teaching zakat al-fitr. The commentary provides hadith evidence: the first evidence from Abu Musa and Hudhayfah shows the Companions reported four takbirs (including the opening takbir) in each rak'ah; the second evidence is from the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (a Tabi'i's report). The text also cites al-Shafi'i's proof that the prayer was before the sermon, but that does not contradict the Hanafi position. Raising hands is established from 'Umar's practice, though the chain is munqati'. The jahr (aloud recitation) is supported by the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. All these rulings are sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms
تَكْبِيرَةُ الْإِحْرَامِ (takbirat al-ihram): The initial 'Allahu Akbar' that begins the prayer and makes it valid.
الْخُطْبَةُ (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered after the Eid prayer, consisting of two parts with a short sitting in between.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, how many extra takbirs (excluding the opening takbir and the takbir for ruku') are there in the first rak'ah of Eid prayer?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Six

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi Eid prayer has three extra takbirs after the opening in each rak'ah, jahr recitation, and the khutbah after the prayer—all sunnah mu'akkadah.

Recommended Acts on the Day of Eid al-Adha
List of recommended acts with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four recommended acts on the day of Eid al-Adha according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence for each from the prophetic practice.

Core Idea
On Eid al-Adha, delay eating until after prayer and go to the musalla reciting takbir—distinct from Eid al-Fitr.

The day of Eid al-Adha is marked by distinct sunan that enhance its spiritual atmosphere. This lesson examines the four recommended acts (mustahabbat) listed in al-Quduri: ghusl, perfume, delaying eating, and walking to the musalla with takbir. Understanding these acts and their proofs helps you practice Eid in accordance with the prophetic model.

Guided Path
1
List the four recommended acts
Identify each act: ghusl, tatayyub (perfume), delaying eating until after the Eid prayer, and going to the musalla while reciting takbir. Note that ghusl and perfume are general sunan, while the latter two have specific timing.
All four are mustahabb (sunnah muakkadah) on Adha.
2
Locate evidence for delaying eating
Read the hadith of Buraydah: the Prophet would not eat on Adha until he returned from the prayer and ate from his sacrifice. This is explicit proof for delaying.
On Fitr, he would eat before prayer, showing the contrast.
3
Locate evidence for takbir while walking
Read the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet would recite takbir from the time he left home until reaching the musalla. This shows the recommended practice.
Takbir is audible, not silent.
4
Identify proofs for ghusl and perfume
The matn directly states these as recommended. Their proof lies in general narrations about cleanliness and adornment for Eid, though not explicitly quoted in this passage.
Other hadith, e.g., the Prophet would bathe on Eid, support ghusl.
5
Contrast with Eid al-Fitr
On Fitr, eating sweet dates before prayer is sunnah. On Adha, one delays until after prayer, preferably from the udhiyya. Understand the wisdom: on Adha, the sacrifice is the first food.
This differentiation is well-established in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ فِي يَوْمِ الْأَضْحَى أَنْ يَغْتَسِلَ وَيَتَطَيَّبَ وَيُؤَخِّرَ الْأَكْلَ حَتَّى يَفْرُغَ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ وَيَتَوَجَّهَ إِلَى الْمُصَلَّى وَهُوَ يُكَبِّرُ. وَجْهٌ: (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ فِي يَوْمِ الْأَضْحَى أَنْ يَغْتَسِلَ ثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ لَا يَخْرُجُ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ حَتَّى يَطْعَمَ، وَكَانَ لَا يَأْكُلُ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ شَيْئًا حَتَّى يَرْجِعَ فَيَأْكُلَ مِنْ أُضْحِيَّتِهِ (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ: 6 – كِتَابُ الْعِيدَيْنِ، رَقْم 1715, سُنَنُ الْبَيْهَقِيِّ: بَابُ يَتْرُكُ الْأَكْلَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ حَتَّى يَرْجِعَ، رَقْم 6161) وَجْهٌ: (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَتَوَجَّهَ إِلَى الْمُصَلَّى وَهُوَ يُكَبِّرُ عَنْ أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عُمَرَ أَخْبَرَهُ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ يُكَبِّرُ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ مِنْ حِينِ يَخْرُجُ مِنْ بَيْتِهِ حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ الْمُصَلَّى (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ: كِتَابُ الْعِيدَيْنِ رَقْم 1714، مُسْتَدْرَكُ الْحَاكِمِ كِتَابُ صَلَاةِ الْعِيدَيْنِ، رَقْم 1105)
And it is recommended on the day of Adha to bathe, apply perfume, delay eating until he finishes the prayer, and to go to the musalla while making takbir. Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing 'it is recommended on the day of Adha to bathe': 'Abdullah ibn Buraydah narrated from his father that the Prophet, peace be upon him, would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten, and he would not eat anything on the day of Nahr (Adha) until he returned and ate from his sacrifice (Sunan al-Daraqutni: 6 – Book of the Two Eids, no. 1715; Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter he leaves eating on the day of Nahr until he returns, no. 6161). Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing 'he goes to the musalla while making takbir': That 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar informed him that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, would make takbir on the day of Fitr from the time he left his house until he came to the musalla (Sunan al-Daraqutni: Book of the Two Eids no. 1714; Mustadrak al-Hakim: Book of the Eid Prayer, no. 1105).
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage lists four recommended acts (mustahabbat) for the day of Eid al-Adha: 1) taking a bath (ghusl), 2) applying perfume (tayyib), 3) delaying eating until after the Eid prayer (contrary to Eid al-Fitr where it is sunnah to eat before prayer), and 4) going to the prayer ground (musalla) while reciting the takbir aloud. The evidence for ghusl is derived from the general practice and the hadith about not eating on Adha until after prayer, implying he would bathe before. The evidence for delaying eating is explicit in the hadith of Buraydah regarding Nahr. The evidence for reciting takbir while going to the musalla is from the practice of Ibn 'Umar reporting the Prophet. These acts are sunnah mu'akkadah and enhance the celebration of the Eid.

Key Terms
الْمُصَلَّى (al-musalla): The designated prayer ground outside the mosque where the Eid prayer is performed.
التَّطَيُّب (al-tatayyub): Applying perfume or scent, which is recommended on Eid days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT recommended on the day of Eid al-Adha according to this passage?
A) Taking a bath (ghusl).
B) Applying perfume.
C) Eating dates before going to prayer.
D) Walking to the musalla while reciting takbir.

Key Takeaway
The four sunnan of Eid al-Adha—ghusl, perfume, delaying eating, and takbir while walking—are mustahabb acts that follow the Prophet's practice and deepen the festive spirit.

Solar Eclipse Prayer: Silent vs Loud Recitation (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Ruling on solar eclipse prayer with intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on solar eclipse prayer and explain the intra-madhhab dispute over recitation, citing the proofs for each position and identifying the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
In solar eclipse prayer, the Hanafi relied-upon position is silent recitation, based on explicit hadith of silence.

Eclipse prayer is a sunnah muakkadah with specific rules. One key issue is whether the imam recites silently or aloud. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position—mainly silent—and the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his students, supported by multiple hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
The text describes solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). It is a sunnah muakkadah with two rak'ahs, lengthened recitation, and a requirement for the imam. Identify the overall hukm level.
Hanafi school considers it sunnah muakkadah, not fard.
2
State the two intra-Hanafi positions on recitation
Abu Hanifa holds that the imam recites silently (ikhfa'). Abu Yusuf holds that he recites aloud (jahr). Imam Muhammad also considers loud recitation afdal (but not the mufta bihi).
This is a dispute within the Hanafi school, not with another madhhab.
3
Analyze the proof for silent recitation
Three hadith are cited: (1) Samurah: 'we did not hear a sound' (Abu Dawood 1184). (2) Aisha: 'I estimated his recitation as Surah al-Baqarah' (Abu Dawood 1187). (3) Ibn Abbas: 'I did not hear a single letter' (Musnad Ahmad 2673). These indicate silent recitation.
These hadith are specific to solar eclipse.
4
Analyze the proof for loud recitation
Aisha reported: 'The Prophet recited aloud in the lunar eclipse prayer' (Bukhari 1065). Abu Yusuf uses this hadith, analogizing from lunar to solar eclipse.
The opposing hadith is about lunar eclipse (khusuf), not solar (kusuf).
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference) and mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is silent recitation. The direct silence reports for solar eclipse are stronger than the analogy from lunar. Later Hanafi authorities prefer Abu Hanifa's view.
Despite the dispute, the madhhab's operative ruling is silent recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الْقِرَاءَةَ فِيهِمَا وَيُخْفِي الإِمَامُ الْقِرَاءَةَ اعَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: كَسَفَتِ الشَّمْسُ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَخَرَجَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَصَلَّى قرائت ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک البتہ امام محمد کے نزدیک جہرا افضل ہے۔
Chapter of the Eclipse Prayer: He lengthens the recitation in them (the two rak'ahs). The imam conceals the recitation according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf – may Allah have mercy on him – said: He recites aloud in it. And he makes supplication after it until the sun clears. The one who leads the people in prayer is the imam who leads them in Friday prayer. If he is not present, the people pray individually. And the proof for the length and concealment: (1) Samurah said: While I and a boy from the Ansar were shooting at two targets... so he prayed, and he stood with us longer than any prayer he ever stood with us, we did not hear a sound from him... then he bowed... then he prostrated... then he did the same in the second rak'ah. (2) From Aisha: The sun eclipsed in the time of the Messenger of Allah, so he came out and led the people in prayer; he stood and I estimated his recitation and I thought he recited Surah al-Baqarah. (3) From Ibn Abbas: I prayed with the Messenger of Allah during the eclipse, and I did not hear from him a single letter of the Quran. Proof for the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): From Aisha: The Prophet recited aloud in the lunar eclipse prayer. And the proof for supplication after until the sun clears: From Abu Bakrah: The sun and moon are two signs of Allah, they do not eclipse for anyone's death; when that happens, pray and supplicate until what is with you is removed. Principle: The solar eclipse prayer has silent recitation according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but according to Imam Muhammad, loud recitation is more virtuous.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage presents the rulings on solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) from the Hanafi matn, along with proofs (hadith) and an intra-madhhab dispute. The matn states two main rulings: (1) The imam prolongs the recitation in both rak'ahs, and according to Abu Hanifa, he recites silently (ikhfa'), while Abu Yusuf holds that he recites aloud (jahr). (2) After the prayer, the imam and congregation make supplication until the sun reappears. The imam for this prayer is the same as the Friday prayer imam; if absent, people pray individually. The commentary then provides hadith proofs. For Abu Hanifa's position of silent recitation, three hadith are cited: the hadith of Samurah indicating that the Prophet's recitation was inaudible; the hadith of Aisha estimating his recitation as Surah al-Baqarah without mention of hearing it; and the hadith of Ibn Abbas explicitly stating he did not hear a single letter. For the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad — though only Abu Yusuf is named in the matn), a hadith from Aisha states that the Prophet recited aloud in the lunar eclipse prayer (salat al-khusuf), analogously applied to solar eclipse. The proof for supplication comes from a hadith commanding prayer and supplication until the eclipse clears. The Urdu note clarifies that silent recitation is the position of Abu Hanifa, while Imam Muhammad considers loud recitation superior, but the madhhab's relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa. The passage ends with the rule that the imam for eclipse prayer is the Friday imam; if absent, individuals pray separately.

Key Terms
الكُسُوف (al-kusūf): Solar eclipse in the context of this chapter; the prayer prescribed for it.
سُرّي (sirrī): Silent recitation in prayer, where the imam recites the Quran audibly to himself but not aloud.
جَهَر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayer, where the imam recites audibly so others can hear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab's mufta bihi (relied-upon position), how should the imam recite in the solar eclipse prayer?
A) Aloud (jahr)
B) Silently (sirr)
C) In a whisper not audible to anyone
D) It is optional, the imam chooses

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position for solar eclipse prayer is silent recitation, supported by explicit hadith and preferred by later authorities.

Eclipse Prayer: No Congregation in Lunar Eclipse, No Sermon
Stating rulings for solar and lunar eclipse prayers with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for lunar eclipse congregation and eclipse sermon, and identify the hadith evidence that supports each.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, lunar eclipse prayer is performed individually, and no sermon is given in any eclipse prayer.

Eclipse prayers are a sunnah act established by the Prophet ﷺ. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between solar and lunar eclipses in form and content. This lesson examines two specific rulings from the Quduri matn: that the lunar eclipse prayer is not performed in congregation, and that no sermon is delivered after any eclipse prayer. These rulings are derived from the Prophet's practice and are supported by clear hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the matn carefully to extract the two core hukms: (1) no congregation in lunar eclipse, (2) no sermon in any eclipse prayer.
The matn uses 'khusuf' for lunar and 'kusuf' for solar eclipse.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
The author cites three hadith faces (wajh). Face (1) from Abu Bakra proves no congregation in lunar eclipse by inferring from the Prophet's action. Faces (2) and (3) prove no sermon by showing the Prophet did not give a sermon after the prayer itself.
The hadith are from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
For the congregation ruling: the Prophet led a congregation for solar eclipse but not for lunar; the general command 'sallu' applies to both but the specific action differentiates. For the sermon: the Prophet's sermon after solar eclipse was separate from the prayer, not a part of it.
Hanafi usul: the Prophet's action (fi'l) is a source of law.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools permit congregation for lunar eclipse and consider a sermon sunnah. The Hanafi position is based on the absence of transmitted practice.
This becomes relevant when following a different school in a mixed community.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is exactly as stated in the matn: no congregation in lunar eclipse, no sermon in any eclipse prayer.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the operative fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْكُسُوفِ
وَلَيْسَ فِي خُسُوفِ الْقَمَرِ جَمَاعَةٌ وَإِنَّمَا يُصَلِّي كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ لِنَفْسِهِ . وَلَيْسَ فِي الْكُسُوفِ خُطْبَةٌ
الوجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وليس في خسوف القمر جماعة عن أبي بكرة قال: كنا عند رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فانكسفت الشمس، فقام النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يجر رداءه، حتى دخل المسجد، فدخلنا، فصلى بنا ركعتين، حتى انجلت الشمس فقال: إن الشمس والقمر لا ينكسفان لموت أحد، فإذا رأيتموهما فصلوا وادعوا حتى يكشف ما بكم (بخاري: باب الصلاة في كسوف الشمس، رقم 1040، سنن أبي داود: باب من قال أربع ركعات، رقم 1185)
وجه: (2) الحديث لثبوت وليس في الكسوف خطبة عن أبي بكرة فقال: إن الشمس والقمر آيتان من آيات الله، وإنهما لا يخسفان لموت أحد، وإذا كان ذاك فصلوا وادعوا حتى يكشف ما بكم (بخاري: باب الصلاة في كسوف القمر، رقم 1063)
وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت وليس في الكسوف خطبة عن أسماء قالت: فانصرف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقد تجلت الشمس فخطب فحمد الله بما هو أهله ثم قال أما بعد (بخاري: باب قول الإمام في خطبة الكسوف أما بعد، رقم 1061)
اصول: نماز کسوف میں خطبہ اور نماز خسوف میں جماعت ثابت نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of the Eclipse Prayer: There is no congregation in the lunar eclipse, and each person prays individually. And there is no sermon in the eclipse. Face (1): The hadith proving 'There is no congregation in lunar eclipse' from Abu Bakra: ... Face (2): The hadith proving 'There is no sermon in eclipse' ... Face (3): The hadith proving 'There is no sermon in eclipse' from Asma: ... Principle: The sermon in solar eclipse prayer and congregation in lunar eclipse prayer are not established.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage from the Quduri matn states two rulings regarding eclipse prayers: (1) The lunar eclipse (khusuf) prayer is not performed in congregation; each person prays individually. (2) Neither the solar nor lunar eclipse prayer has a sermon (khutbah). The author then provides three hadith proofs: The first hadith from Abu Bakra shows that the Prophet led a congregational prayer for the solar eclipse, from which it is inferred that for lunar eclipse there is no congregation. The second hadith likewise shows no sermon. The third hadith from Asma shows that even when the Prophet gave a sermon after a solar eclipse, it was not part of the prayer itself but a separate address. The Urdu principle concludes that the sermon in solar eclipse prayer and congregation in lunar eclipse prayer are not established in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse
خطبة (khutbah): Sermon after the prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is performed in congregation like solar eclipse.
B) Each person prays individually; there is no congregation.
C) It is permissible to pray either individually or in congregation.
D) It is obligatory to pray in congregation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between solar and lunar eclipse prayers: only solar eclipse prayer is performed in congregation, and no sermon is delivered after any eclipse prayer.

Istisqa: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Congregational Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istisqa prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on istisqa prayer, identify the proofs for each, and evaluate the practical difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa sees istisqa as du'a alone; the Sahibayn include two rak'ahs with khutbah.

The prayer for rain (istisqa) is a recognized practice in Islam, but its format is disputed even within the Hanafi school. In this passage, we see a clear intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa holds that there is no sunnah prayer in congregation—only supplication and seeking forgiveness—while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), maintain that the imam leads two rak'ahs aloud, followed by a khutbah. Let us examine their evidence and the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify exactly what Abu Hanifa says about istisqa: no sunnah prayer in congregation, only du'a and istighfar; individual prayer is permissible.
2
State the Sahibayn's position
Identify the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the imam leads two rak'ahs aloud, then delivers a khutbah facing the qibla.
3
Identify the proof for Abu Hanifa
Locate the Quranic verse (71:10-9) and the hadith of Anas that the author cites as support for Abu Hanifa's view.
The verse emphasizes istighfar; the hadith shows the Prophet making du'a without mentioning congregational prayer.
4
Identify the proof for the Sahibayn
Locate the hadith of Abbad ibn Tamim and the hadith of Aisha that support the Sahibayn's view.
These hadiths explicitly mention two rak'ahs with jahr and a khutbah.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Explain how the differing positions affect actual practice: Abu Hanifa recommends only du'a; the Sahibayn prescribe a congregational prayer.
Later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةِ الِاسْتِسْقَاءِ
قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ لَيْسَ فِي الِاسْتِسْقَاءِ صَلَاةٌ مَسْنُونَةٌ فِي جَمَاعَةٍ وَإِنَّمَا الِاسْتِسْقَاءُ الدُّعَاءُ وَالِاسْتِغْفَارُ فَإِنْ صَلَّى النَّاسُ وُحْدَانًا جَازَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يُصَلِّى الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَيَجْهَرُ فِيهِمَا بِالْقِرَاءَةِ ثُمَّ يَخْطُبُ وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْقِبْلَةَ بِالدُّعَاءِ
الوجه: (1) الاية لثبوت قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ لَيْسَ فِي الِاسْتِسْقَاءِ صَلَاةٌ مَسْنُونَةٌ 
فَقُلْتُ اسْتَغْفِرُوا رَبَّكُمْ إِنَّهُ كَانَ غَفَّارًا (سورة نوح 71:10-9)
الوجه: (2) الحديث لثبوت قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ لَيْسَ فِي الِاسْتِسْقَاءِ عن أنس بن مالك: أن رجلا دخل المسجد يوم جمعة من باب كان نحو دار القضاء، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قائم يخطب، ... فرفع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يديه، ثم قال: اللهم أغثنا (بخاري: باب الاستسقاء في خطبة الجمعة غير مستقبل القبلة، رقم 1014 مسلم: باب الدعاء في الاستسقاء، رقم 897 سنن أبي داود: باب رفع اليدين في الاستسقاء، رقم 1175)
الوجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ صَلَّى النَّاسُ وُحْدَانًا جَازَ عن عباد بن تميم، عن عمه قال: خرج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يستسقي فتوجه إلى القبلة يدعو، وحول رداءه، ثم صلى ركعتين، جهر فيهما بالقراءة (بخاري: باب الجهر بالقراءة في الاستسقاء، رقم 1024, مسلم: كتاب صلاة الاستسقاء، رقم 894 سنن أبي داود: جماع أبواب صلاة الاستسقاء وتفريعها، رقم 1161)
الوجه: (4) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يَخْطُبُ وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْقِبْلَةَ بِالدُّعَاءِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يُصَلِّي الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ عن عائشة قالت: شكا الناس إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قحوط المطر، فأمر منبر فوضع له في المصلى ... فقعد على المنبر فكبر، وحمد الله عز وجل (سنن أبي داود: باب رفع اليدين في الاستسقاء، رقم 1173)
اصول: استقاء کے معنی ہیں بارش طلب کرنا، امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک استسقاء کے لئے نماز لازم نہیں ہے صرف دعا بھی کر لیں تو کافی ہے، جبکہ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ استقاء کی دور کعت مسنون ہے۔
Chapter of the Prayer for Rain: Abu Hanifa said: There is no sunnah prayer in congregation for rain-seeking; rather rain-seeking is supplication and seeking forgiveness. If people pray individually, it is permissible. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The imam leads the people in two rak'ahs, reciting aloud in them, then he delivers a sermon and faces the qibla in supplication. Face (1): The verse proving Abu Hanifa's statement that there is no sunnah prayer for rain-seeking: 'Then I said: Seek forgiveness of your Lord, indeed He is Oft-Forgiving.' (Surah Nuh 71:10-9) Face (2): The hadith proving Abu Hanifa's statement from Anas... Face (3): The hadith proving 'If people pray individually, it is permissible' from Abbad... Face (4): The hadith proving 'Then he delivers a sermon and faces the qibla in supplication' and the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad from Aisha... Principle: Istisqa means seeking rain. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, prayer is not necessary for istisqa; supplication alone is sufficient. According to the Sahibayn, two rak'ahs are sunnah.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the prayer for rain (istisqa). The matn states Abu Hanifa's position: there is no sunnah congregational prayer; rather, istisqa consists of du'a and istighfar. If individuals pray alone, it is permissible. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the imam leads two rak'ahs with jahr, then gives a khutbah facing qibla. The author then provides evidence: an ayah from Surah Nuh emphasizing istighfar, two hadiths supporting Abu Hanifa (the Prophet's practice of du'a without congregational prayer), and two hadiths supporting the Sahibayn (the Prophet leading two rak'ahs and delivering a khutbah). The Urdu principle summarizes that Abu Hanifa does not require prayer, while the Sahibayn consider two rak'ahs sunnah.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa): Seeking rain through prayer and supplication
مسنونة (masnunah): Sunnah (recommended) prayer
صاحبين (sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The imam leads two rak'ahs with jahr, then delivers a khutbah facing qibla.
C) People should pray individually if they wish.
D) The imam should give a khutbah without any prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, istisqa includes a two-rak'ah congregational prayer with khutbah according to the mufta bihi (Sahibayn), though Abu Hanifa held it is only du'a.

6 min
The Ruling of Tarawih (Qiyam Ramadan) and Its Proofs
Commentary on Tarawih with multiple proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih (number of rak'ahs, congregation, timing) and cite the primary proofs from hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs of sunnah mu'akkadah prayed in congregation in Ramadan, established by the Prophet's action and the consensus of the early Caliphs.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on Tarawih (Qiyam Ramadan) as presented in Al-Quduri's matn. The text rules that it is recommended (mustahabb) for the community to gather after Isha in Ramadan for twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih, followed by Witr in congregation. The commentary supports this ruling with multiple hadith and the practice of the Companions, especially Umar and Ali. By the end, you will understand the legal basis for the 20-rak'ah Tarawih and how the Hanafi school reconciles the various narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Locate the act being ruled upon: Tarawih (Qiyam Ramadan). The ruling is 'mustahabb' (recommended/sunnah mu'akkadah). Note that it is not fard or wajib.
The Prophet stopped congregational prayer fearing obligation, indicating recommendation.
2
Extract the Specifics from the Matn
The matn specifies: 5 tarwihas, each with 2 salams (total 20 rak'ahs), after Isha, with a sitting break between tarwihas, then Witr in congregation. Note that Witr is only in congregation during Ramadan.
Each tarwiha = 2 rak'ahs × 2 salams = 4 rak'ahs? Actually 5 tarwihas × 4 rak'ahs = 20, but standard is 2 rak'ahs per salam. Clarify: 5 tarwihas × 2 salams each = 10 salams = 20 rak'ahs.
3
Trace the First Proof: Prophet's Night Prayer (Aisha)
The hadith of Aisha (Bukhari/Muslim) shows the Prophet prayed in congregation on several nights but stopped fearing it would become obligatory. The narration states he died and the practice remained as it was, indicating it is recommended, not obligatory.
This proves the recommendation of congregational Tarawih, not the number.
4
Analyze the Explicit Number Proof: Ibn Abbas's Hadith
Ibn Abbas (Bayhaqi) reports the Prophet prayed 20 rak'ahs and Witr in Ramadan without congregation. This establishes the number of rak'ahs for Tarawih.
Even though the Prophet prayed alone, the number is established.
5
Understand the Companions' Practice as Evidence
The action of Umar (giving breaks between tarwihas) and Ali (leading 20 rak'ahs and Witr) shows the established practice of 20 rak'ahs in congregation. This is used as supporting evidence (qawl al-sahabi).
The commentary also reconciles Aisha's hadith about 8 rak'ahs as referring to Tahajjud, not Tarawih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ قِيَامِ شَهْرٍ رَمَضَانَ
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِلنَّاسِ أَنْ يَجْتَمِعُوا فِي شَهْرٍ رَمَضَانَ بَعْدَ الْعِشَاءِ فَيُصَلِّيَ بِهِيمُ الْإِمَامُ خَمْسَ تَرْوِيحَاتٍ - فِي كُلِّ تَرْوِيحَةٍ تَسْلِيمَتَانِ
وَيَجْلِسُ بَيْنَ كُلِّ تَرْوِيحَتَيْنِ مِقْدَارَ تَرْوِيحَةٍ ثُمَّ يُوتِرُ بِهِمْ
وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِلنَّاسِ أَنْ يَجْتَمِعُوا فِي شَهْرٍ رَمَضَانَ \ أَنَّ عَائِشَةَ أَخْبَرَتْهُ: «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم خَرَجَ لَيْلَةً مِنْ جَوْفِ اللَّيْلِ، فَصَلَّى فِي الْمَسْجِدِ، وَصَلَّى رِجَالٌ بِصَلَاتِهِ، فَأَصْبَحَ النَّاسُ فَتَحَدَّثُوا فَاجْتَمَعَ أَكْثَرُ مِنْهُمْ فَصَلَّوْا مَعَهُ، فَأَصْبَحَ النَّاسُ فَتَحَدَّثُوا، فَكَفَرَ أَهْلُ الْمَسْجِدِ مِنَ اللَّيْلَةِ الثَّالِثَةِ، فَخَرَجَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَصَلَّى فَصَلَّوْا بِصَلَاتِهِ، فَلَمَّا كَانَتِ اللَّيْلَةُ الرَّابِعَةُ عَجَزَ الْمَسْجِدُ عَنْ أَهْلِهِ، حَتَّى خَرَجَ لِصَلَاةِ الصُّبْحِ، فَلَمَّا قَضَى الْفَجْرَ أَقْبَلَ عَلَى النَّاسِ، فَتَشَهَّدَ ثُمَّ قَالَ: أَمَّا بَعْدُ، فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يَخْفَ عَلَيَّ مَكَانُكُمْ، وَلَكِنِّي خَشِيتُ أَنْ تُفْتَرَضَ عَلَيْكُمْ فَتَعْجِزُوا عَنْهَا. فَتُوُفِّيَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَالْأَمْرُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ، (بخاري بَابُ فَضْلِ مَنْ قَامَ رَمَضَانَ، نمبر 2012 / مسلم شریف، بَاب التَّرْغِيبِ فِي قِيَامِ رَمَضَانَ وَهُوَ التَّرَاوِيحُ، نمبر 761) وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِلنَّاسِ أَنْ يَجْتَمِعُوا فِي شَهْرِ رَمَضَانَ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ : " كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُصَلِّي فِي شَهْرِ رَمَضَانَ فِي غَيْرِ جَمَاعَةٍ بِعِشْرِينَ رَكْعَةٍ، وَالْوِتْرِ سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَا رُوِيَ فِي عَدَدِ رَكَعَاتِ الْقِيَامِ فِي شَهْرِ رَمَضَانَ، نمبر 4615)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِلنَّاسِ أَنْ يَجْتَمِعُوا فِي شَهْرِ رَمَضَانَ \ أَنَّ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: «سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ لِرَمَضَانَ : مَنْ قَامَهُ إِيمَانًا وَاحْتِسَابًا غُفِرَ لَهُ مَا تَقَدَّمَ مِنْ ذَنْبِهِ،(بخاري بَابُ فَضْلِ مَنْ قَامَ رَمَضَانَ ، نمبر 2008 / مسلم شریف، بَاب التَّرْغِيبِ فِي قِيَامِ رَمَضَانَ وَهُوَ التَّرَاوِيحُ ، نمبر 759/سنن ابوداود بَابٌ فِي قِيَام شَهْرٍ رَمَضَانَ، غبر (1373) وجه : (۱) عمل الصحابي لثبوت وَيَجْلِسُ بَيْنَ كُلِّ تَرْوِيحَتَيْنِ مِقْدَارَ تَرْوِيحَةٍ \ كَانَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ في يُرَوَحْنَا فِي رَمَضَانَ، يَعْنِي بَيْنَ التَّرْوِيحَتَيْنِ قَدْرَ مَا يَذْهَبُ الرَّجُلُ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ إِلَى سَلْعِ،(سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَا رُوِيَ فِي عَدَدِ رَكَعَاتِ الْقِيَامِ فِي شَهْرِ رَمَضَانَ، نمبر 4622) اصول : قیام رمضان سے مراد تراویح ہے، کیونکہ مسلم شریف میں" باب الترغیب فی قیام رمضان وہو التراویح" باب باندھا ہے۔
وَلَا يُصَلِّى الوثرَ فِي جَمَاعَةٍ فِي غَيْرِ شَهْرٍ رَمَضَانَ
وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَجْلِسُ بَيْنَ كُلِ تَرْوِيحَتَيْنِ مِقْدَارَ تَرْوِيحَةٍ \ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ: «أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَكْرَهُ أَنْ يَقُولَ بَيْنَ التَّرْوِيحَتَيْنِ الصَّلَاةُ ، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، في الصَّلَاةِ بَيْنَ التراويح، نمبر 7730)
وجه (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَجْلِسُ بَيْنَ كُلِّ تَرْوِيحَتَيْنِ مِقْدَارَ تَرْوِيحَةٍ \ عَنْ عَلِي هِ قَالَ: " دَعَا الْقُرَّاءَ فِي رَمَضَانَ فَأَمَرَ مِنْهُمْ رَجُلًا يُصَلِّي بِالنَّاسِ عِشْرِينَ رَكْعَةً " قَالَ : وَكَانَ عَلِيٌّ له يُوتِرُ بِهِمْ، (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَا رُوِيَ فِي عَدَدِ رَكَعَاتِ الْقِيَامِ فِي شَهْرٍ رَمَضَانَ، نمبر 4620) اصول : خلیفہ ثانی حضرت عمر اور حضرت علی کے کلام اور بھی دیگر کبار صحابہ کے عمل سے یہ ثابت ہے کہ تراویح بیس رکعت ہے۔ اصول : حضرت عائشہ کی روایت جو رمضان اور غیر رمضان دونوں معمولات کو بتاتے ہیں اس سے مراد تہجد ہے ، جو آٹھ رکعت ہے، اور تراویح بیس رکعت ہے، ورنہ حضرت عائشہ پر بہتان لازم ہو گا کہ ان کے سامنے حضرت عمر نے بیس رکعت تراویح پڑھوائی، اور حضرت عائشہ حجرہ میں موجود تھی، اگر عمر رض کا عمل غلط ہو تا تو حضرت عائشہ خاموش نہ رہتیں۔
Chapter of the Night Prayer of Ramadan. It is recommended for the people to gather in Ramadan after Isha, and the Imam prays with them five tarwihas, in each tarwiha two salams. And he sits between every two tarwihas for the duration of a tarwiha, then he prays Witr with them. Evidence: (1) The hadith for the establishment of 'It is recommended for the people to gather in Ramadan' that Aisha informed him: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) went out one night in the middle of the night and prayed in the mosque, and men prayed with his prayer. In the morning the people spoke, and more of them gathered and prayed with him. In the morning the people spoke, and the people of the mosque crowded on the third night, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) went out and prayed, and they prayed with his prayer. When it was the fourth night, the mosque was overwhelmed with its people, until he went out for the Fajr prayer. When he finished Fajr, he faced the people, recited the tashahhud, then said: 'Indeed, your place was not hidden from me, but I feared that it would be prescribed upon you and you would be unable to do it.' Then the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) died and the matter remained as it was. (Bukhari, Chapter on the Virtue of Whoever Stands Ramadan, no. 2012 / Muslim, Chapter on Encouragement of Standing Ramadan, which is Tarawih, no. 761) Evidence: (2) The hadith for the establishment of 'It is recommended...' from Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray in Ramadan without congregation, twenty rak'ahs and Witr.' (Sunan Bayhaqi, Chapter on What is Narrated about the Number of Rak'ahs of Qiyam in Ramadan, no. 4615) Evidence: (3) The hadith for the establishment... that Abu Huraira said: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say regarding Ramadan: Whoever stands it with faith and seeking reward, his past sins will be forgiven.' (Bukhari, Chapter..., no. 2008 / Muslim, Chapter..., no. 759 / Sunan Abu Dawud, Chapter on Standing Ramadan, [?] 1373) Evidence: (1) The action of the Companion for the establishment of 'He sits between every two tarwihas for the duration of a tarwiha' that Umar ibn al-Khattab used to give us a break in Ramadan, meaning between the two tarwihas for the time it takes a man to go from the mosque to Sal'. (Sunan Bayhaqi, Chapter..., no. 4622) Principle: Qiyam Ramadan refers to Tarawih, because Muslim entitled a chapter 'Chapter on Encouragement of Standing Ramadan which is Tarawih.' And Witr is not prayed in congregation outside of Ramadan. Evidence: (2) The statement of the Companion for the establishment... from Sa'id ibn Jubayr that he disliked saying 'prayer' between the tarwihas. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, On the Prayer between Tarawih, no. 7730) Evidence: (3) The statement of the Companion for the establishment... from Ali (may Allah honor him) who said: 'He called the reciters in Ramadan and ordered a man from among them to pray with the people twenty rak'ahs.' He said: 'And Ali used to pray Witr with them.' (Sunan Bayhaqi, Chapter..., no. 4620) Principle: The action of the second caliph Umar and Ali and other senior Companions establishes that Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs. Principle: The hadith of Aisha which describes the practice in both Ramadan and non-Ramadan refers to Tahajjud, which is eight rak'ahs, while Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs; otherwise it would be an accusation against Aisha, for Umar led twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih in her presence while she was in her chamber, and if Umar's action were wrong, Aisha would not have remained silent.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is from the matn of Al-Quduri and its commentary, addressing the rulings of Tarawih (Qiyam Ramadan). The matn states that it is mustahabb (recommended) for people to gather in congregation after Isha prayer during Ramadan, and the Imam leads them in five tarwihas, each tarwiha consisting of two rak'ahs (hence ten rak'ahs per tarwiha? Wait: five tarwihas, each with two salam, so two rak'ahs per salam? Actually the phrase 'in each tarwiha two salams' means each tarwiha has two units of two rak'ahs? No, standard Hanafi practice is that Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs, prayed as 10 salams of 2 rak'ahs each. But here it says five tarwihas, each tarwiha containing two salams, so total 10 salams = 20 rak'ahs. So it aligns. The matn also says the Imam sits between each two tarwihas for the duration of a tarwiha, then prays Witr with them. The commentary provides proofs: The hadith of Aisha (Bukhari and Muslim) shows the Prophet prayed in congregation but stopped fearing it would become obligatory, and it remained as such after his death, proving the recommendation. The hadith of Ibn Abbas (Bayhaqi) explicitly states the Prophet prayed 20 rak'ahs alone. The hadith of Abu Huraira encourages standing Ramadan. The action of Umar (reported by Bayhaqi) shows the practice of breaking between tarwihas. The commentary also states that Witr is not prayed in congregation outside Ramadan, citing the statement of Sa'id ibn Jubayr and the action of Ali. The usul note clarifies that Aisha's hadith about the Prophet's night prayer (8 rak'ahs) refers to Tahajjud, not Tarawih, resolving the apparent contradiction. This is essential Hanafi fiqh: Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs, sunnah mu'akkadah, prayed in congregation in Ramadan.

Key Terms
تراویح (tarāwīḥ): The night prayer of Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs performed in congregation after Isha, with breaks (tarwihas) between sets.
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayers, typically 3 rak'ahs. In Ramadan, it is prayed in congregation after Tarawih; otherwise it is not prayed in congregation.
قیام رمضان (qiyām ramaḍān): Literally 'standing of Ramadan', used synonymously with Tarawih in the Hanafi school.
ترویحة (tarwīḥa): A break or rest period between sets of Tarawih; also used to refer to a set of four rak'ahs (two salams) in some contexts.
مستحب (mustaḥabb): Recommended; a ruling level between sunnah and mubah. In Hanafi fiqh, often synonymous with sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Quduri, how many rak'ahs are prayed in Tarawih?
A) 8 rak'ahs
B) 20 rak'ahs
C) 12 rak'ahs
D) 16 rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Tarawih consists of 20 rak'ahs prayed in congregation after Isha in Ramadan, based on the practice of the Prophet and the Caliphs, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas explicitly states 20 rak'ahs.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Method of Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer)
Matn and proofs for the fear prayer when battle rages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf for a two-rak'ah prayer and explain how the imam leads two groups, citing the hadith of Ibn 'Umar as proof.

Core Idea
In Fear Prayer, the imam leads one rak'ah with each of two groups; each group completes its second rak'ah alone.

The Fear Prayer (Salat al-Khawf) is a special form of congregational prayer permitted when the enemy is close. The Hanafi school relies on the explicit practice of the Prophet ﷺ as narrated by Ibn 'Umar. In this lesson, we will examine the matn of Al-Quduri, which lays out the method step by step, and the hadith that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Salat al-Khawf is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed practice) performed when fear of the enemy is intense. It is permissible to delay the prayer if fighting is unavoidable.
The ruling is not fard; it is a sunnah that fulfills the obligation of prayer in a state of danger.
2
Describe the division of the army
The imam splits the soldiers into two groups (ta'ifatan). One group stands facing the enemy while the other prays behind the imam.
This ensures continuous defense of the camp.
3
State the prayer sequence for the two groups
The imam leads the first group in one rak'ah (including two sajdas). After raising from the second sajda, that group goes to face the enemy, and the second group comes. The imam leads them in one rak'ah, recites tashahhud, and says salam, but the second group does not yet say salam.
The imam completes his own prayer with the second group.
4
Explain each group's individual completion
The first group returns and prays their second rak'ah individually (without recitation, since they already recited behind the imam). The second group, after the imam's salam, goes to the enemy, and then returns to pray their second rak'ah individually (with recitation).
The first group's individual rak'ah has no qira'ah because they already fulfilled it with the imam; the second group recites because they did not recite during the imam's second rak'ah (they only stood).
5
Note the exceptions for a resident imam and for Maghrib
If the imam is a resident (muqim) and the prayer is four rak'ahs (Zuhr, Asr, Isha), he leads two rak'ahs with each group. For Maghrib (three rak'ahs), he leads two with the first group and one with the second.
Fighting during the prayer invalidates it due to excessive action (amal kathir).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْخَوْفِ
إِذَا اشْتَدَّ الْخَوْفُ جَعَلَ الْإِمَامُ النَّاسَ طَائِفَتَيْنِ طَائِفَةً إِلَى وَجْهِ الْعَدُوِّ وَطَائِفَةً خَلْفَهُ فَيُصَلِّي بِهَذِهِ الطَّائِفَةِ رَكْعَةً وَسَجْدَتَيْنِ فَإِذَا رَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ مِنَ السَّجْدَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ مَضَتْ هَذِهِ الطَّائِفَةُ إِلَى وَجْهِ الْعَدُوِّ وَجَاءَتْ تِلْكَ الطَّائِفَةُ الْأُخْرَى فَيُصَلِّي بِهِمْ رَكْعَةً وَسَجْدَتَيْنِ وَتَشَهَّدَ وَسَلَّمَ وَلَمْ يُسَلِّمُوا وَذَهَبُوا إِلَى وَجْهِ الْعَدُوِّ وَجَاءَتِ الطَّائِفَةُ الْأُولَى فَيُصَلُّونَ وُحْدَانًا رَكْعَةً وَسَجْدَتَيْنِ بِغَيْرِ قِرَاءَةٍ وَتَشَهَّدُوا وَسَلَّمُوا لِأَنَّ صَلَاتَهُمْ قَدْ كَمُلَتْ وَمَضَوْا إِلَى وَجْهِ الْعَدُوِّ وَجَاءَتِ الطَّائِفَةُ الْأُخْرَى فَيُصَلُّونَ رَكْعَةً وَسَجْدَتَيْنِ بِقِرَاءَةٍ فَإِنْ كَانَ الْإِمَامُ مُقِيمًا صَلَّى بِالطَّائِفَةِ الْأُولَى رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَبِالثَّانِيَةِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَيُصَلِّي بِالطَّائِفَةِ الْأُولَى مِنَ الْمَغْرِبِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَبِالثَّانِيَةِ رَكْعَةً وَلَا يُقَاتِلُونَ فِي حَالِ الصَّلَاةِ فَإِنْ قَاتَلُوا بَطَلَتْ صَلَاتُهُمْ.
Chapter of Fear Prayer: When fear is intense, the imam makes the people into two groups: a group towards the enemy and a group behind him. He prays with this group one rak'ah and two prostrations. When he raises his head from the second prostration, this group goes towards the enemy and that other group comes. He prays with them one rak'ah and two prostrations, recites the tashahhud and says the salam, but they do not say salam and they go towards the enemy. The first group comes and they pray individually one rak'ah and two prostrations without recitation, recite tashahhud and say salam because their prayer is complete, and they go towards the enemy. The other group comes and they pray one rak'ah and two prostrations with recitation. If the imam is a resident, he prays with the first group two rak'ahs and with the second two rak'ahs. He prays with the first group of Maghrib two rak'ahs and with the second one rak'ah. They do not fight during the prayer; if they fight, their prayer is invalidated.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This is the matn (core text) of Al-Quduri on the chapter of Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer). It presents the Hanafi ruling on how to pray when the enemy is close and battle is intense. The imam divides the soldiers into two groups: one stands facing the enemy while the other prays one rak'ah with the imam. After the imam raises from the second sajdah, the first group goes to face the enemy and the second group comes. The imam leads them in one rak'ah, then recites tashahhud and salam, but the second group does not yet say salam. They go to the enemy while the first group returns to pray their second rak'ah alone without recitation (since they already recited behind the imam). After completing their prayer, they go to the enemy and the second group returns to pray their second rak'ah alone, this time with recitation. If the imam is a resident (muqim), the prayer is four rak'ahs, so he prays two rak'ahs with each group. For Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one rak'ah with the second. Fighting during the prayer invalidates it; this is because excessive action (amal kathir) breaks the prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
صَلَاةُ الْخَوْفِ (ṣalāt al-khawf): Fear prayer; a specific form of congregational prayer performed during battle or when there is fear of enemy attack.
طَائِفَة (ṭā'ifa): A group of soldiers; in this context, one of the two divisions of the army during the fear prayer.
وَحْدَانًا (waḥdānan): Individually; each person prays alone without an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf for a two-rak'ah prayer, what does the first group do after the imam raises his head from the second sajda?
A) They go to face the enemy.
B) They wait for the imam to say salam.
C) They pray the second rak'ah with the imam.
D) They recite tashahhud and say salam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf, derived from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, ensures that prayer and battle can both be observed by splitting the congregation into two alternating groups, each praying one rak'ah with the imam and completing the rest individually.
