Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Method of Salat al-Khawf with Two Groups
Ruling with proof: method of Salat al-Khawf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf for two groups and apply the rule that excessive action (e.g., fighting) invalidates prayer.

Core Idea
In Salat al-Khawf, the imam leads each group partially; fighting during prayer nullifies it.

This passage from al-Quduri outlines the unique method of Salat al-Khawf (Prayer of Fear) under battle conditions. The prayer is performed in two groups to maintain continuous defense. Understanding this method reveals how the Hanafi school balances obligation with necessity, and why fighting during prayer—a form of excessive action ('amal kathir)—invalidates it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer type and its mandatory nature
Salat al-Khawf is a method for performing the obligatory fard prayer under fear of enemy attack. The obligation remains fard 'ayn, but the procedure is modified.
The prayer is still congregational, but with two groups.
2
Describe the two-group procedure for a two-rak'ah prayer
The imam leads the first group in one rak'ah, then they leave to guard while the second group prays one rak'ah with the imam. The imam completes his prayer, and each group finishes their missing rak'ah individually.
The first group completes their prayer without recitation (since the imam recited for them); the second group recites when they pray alone.
3
Apply the modification for a resident imam and for Maghrib
If the imam is a resident (muqim) praying a four-rak'ah prayer, he prays two rak'ahs with each group. For Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one with the second.
This ensures the imam's total rak'ahs match the regular prayer.
4
Recognize the prohibition of fighting during prayer
The text explicitly states that fighting during prayer invalidates it. This is because fighting involves excessive movement ('amal kathir), which breaks the prayer in Hanafi fiqh.
The principle is general: any excessive extraneous movement nullifies prayer.
5
Connect to the usul principle of 'amal kathir
The ruling that fighting invalidates prayer is derived from the broader usul principle that excessive action (kathir al-'amal) nullifies the prayer. This principle is applied here as a preventive measure.
This principle is rooted in the practice of the Companions and the Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْخَوْفِ
وَجَاءَتْ تِلْكَ الطَّائِفَةُ الْأُخْرَى فَيُصَلِّي بِهِمْ رَكْعَةً وَسَجْدَتَيْنِ وَتَشَهَّدَ وَسَلَّمَ وَلَمْ يُسَلِّمُوا وَذَهَبُوا إلَى وَجْهِ الْعَدُوِّ وَجَاءَتْ الطَّائِفَةُ الْأُولَى فَيُصَلُّونَ وُحْدَانًا رَكْعَةً وَسَجْدَتَيْنِ بِغَيْرِ قِرَاءَةٍ وَتَشَهَّدُوا وَسَلَّمُوا لِأَنَّ صَلَاتَهُمْ قَدْ كَمُلَتْ وَمَضَوْا إِلَى وَجْهِ الْعَدُوِّ وَجَاءَتْ الطَّائِفَةُ الْأُخْرَى فَيُصَلُّونَ رَكْعَةً وَسَجْدَتَيْن بِقِرَاءَةٍ فَإِنْ كَانَ الْإِمَامُ مُقِيمًا صَلَّى بِالطَّائِفَةِ الْأُولَى رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَبِالثَّانِيَةِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ
وَيُصَلِّي بِالطَّائِفَةِ الْأُولَى مِنْ الْمَغْرِبِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَبِالثَّانِيَةِ رَكْعَةً ٣ وَلَا يُقَاتِلُونَ فِي حَالِ الصَّلَاةِ فَإِنْ قَاتَلُوا بَطَلَتْ صَلَاتُهُمْ
مِنْهُمْ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ وَطَائِفَةٌ بِإِزَاءِ الْعَدُوِّ، فَيُصَلِّي الْإِمَامُ بِطَائِفَةِ الَّذِينَ مَعَهُ رَكْعَةً ثُمَّ تَنْصَرِفُ الطَّائِفَةُ الَّذِينَ صَلُّوا مَعَ الْإِمَامِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَتَكَلَّمُوا حَتَّى يَقُومُوا مَقَامَ أَصْحَابِهِمْ، وَتَأْتِي الطَّائِفَةُ الْأُخْرَى فَيُصَلُّونَ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ الرَّكْعَةَ الْأُخْرَى ثُمَّ يَنْصَرِفُونَ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَتَكَلَّمُوا حَتَّى يَقُومُوا فِي مَقَامِ أَصْحَابِهِمْ، وَتَأْتِي الطَّائِفَةُ الْأُولَى حَتَّى يُصَلُّوا رَكْعَةً وُحْدَانًا ثُمَّ يَنْصَرِفُونَ فَيَقُومُونَ مَقَامَ أَصْحَابِهِمْ، وتأتي الطَّائِفَةُ الْأُخْرَى حَتَّى يَقْضُوا الرَّكْعَةَ الَّتِي بَقِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ وَحْدَانًا» (الآثار لمحمد بن الحسن: باب صلاة الخوف، نمبر 194)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي بِالطَّائِفَةِ الْأُولَى مِنْ الْمَغْرِبِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ \ قَالَ: «جَاءَ عُمَرُ يَوْمَ الْخَنْدَقِ فَجَعَلَ يَسُبُّ كُفَّارَ قُرَيْشٍ وَيَقُولُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ، مَا صَلَّيْتُ الْعَصْرَ حَتَّى كَادَتِ الشَّمْسُ أَنْ تَغِيبَ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: وَأَنَا وَاللَّهِ مَا صَلَّيْتُهَا بَعْدُ. قَالَ: فَنَزَلَ إِلَى بُطْحَانَ، فَتَوَضَّأَ وَصَلَّى الْعَصْرَ بَعْدَمَا غَابَتِ الشَّمْسُ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ بَعْدَهَا» (بخاري شريف: باب الصلاة عند مناهضة الحصون ولقاء العدو، نمبر 945 سنن ترمذي: باب ما جاء في الرجل تفوته الصلوات بأيتهن يبدأ ، نمبر 179 سنن نسائي: (٥٥) كيف يقضى الفائت من الصلاة، نمبر 623) وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي بِالطَّائِفَةِ الْأُولَى مِنْ الْمَغْرِبِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ \ وَقَالَ أَنَسٌ حَضَرْتُ عِنْدَ مُنَاهَضَةِ حِصْنِ تُسْتَرَ عِنْدَ إِضَاءَةِ الْفَجْرِ وَاشْتَدَّ اشْتِعَالُ الْقِتَالِ فَلَمْ يَقْدِرُوا عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَلَمْ نُصَلِ إِلَّا بَعْدَ ارْتِفَاعِ النَّهَارِ (بخاري شريف باب الصلاة عند مناهضة الحصون ولقاء العدو، نمبر 945)
اصول: نماز میں عمل کثیر مفسد صلاۃ ہے، لہذا دوران نماز قتال نہیں کریں گے ورنہ نماز باطل ہو جائے گی۔
Chapter of the Prayer of Fear. And that other group came, so he leads them in prayer with one rak'ah and two prostrations, and recites the tashahhud and says salam, and they do not say salam, and they go towards the enemy. And the first group comes, and they pray individually one rak'ah and two prostrations without recitation, and they recite tashahhud and say salam, because their prayer has been completed, and they proceed towards the enemy. And the other group comes, and they pray one rak'ah and two prostrations with recitation. If the imam is a resident, he prays with the first group two rak'ahs and with the second two rak'ahs. And for Maghrib, he prays with the first group two rak'ahs and with the second one rak'ah. And they do not fight during the state of prayer; if they fight, their prayer becomes invalid. ... (Aathar of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan: Chapter of Prayer of Fear, number 194). Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing that he prays with the first group of Maghrib two rak'ahs: 'Umar came on the day of the Trench, cursing the disbelievers of Quraysh... (Bukhari, etc.) (2) The saying of the Companion for establishing that he prays with the first group of Maghrib two rak'ahs: Anas said: I was present at the assault of the fort of Tustar at the break of dawn, and the fighting became intense, so they could not pray until after the day had risen. (Bukhari). Principle: Excessive action in prayer invalidates prayer; therefore, they should not fight during prayer, otherwise their prayer becomes null.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Quduri on the method of Salat al-Khawf (Prayer of Fear). The author describes the procedure: The imam leads one group in one rak'ah of a two-rak'ah prayer, then they leave to face the enemy without completing the prayer. The other group then comes and prays one rak'ah with the imam, and the imam concludes his prayer with tashahhud and salam, while this second group has completed their prayer. Then the first group returns and prays their remaining rak'ah individually without recitation (since the imam already recited) and then make salam. If the imam is a resident (i.e., not traveling), he prays two rak'ahs with each group, effectively completing four rak'ahs. For Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one with the second. The text emphasizes that fighting during the prayer invalidates it, as excessive movement (kathir al-amal) breaks the prayer. This is a fundamental usul principle in Hanafi fiqh. The proof (wajh) includes a hadith from the Battle of the Trench and the practice of the Companions. The author also references the Aathar of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, though other schools differ on the exact method.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): A method of performing obligatory congregational prayer under battle conditions to maintain continuous defense.
عمل کثیر ('Amal Kathir): Excessive physical movement during prayer that invalidates it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Salat al-Khawf for a two-rak'ah prayer when the imam is a traveler, how many rak'ahs does the imam pray with each group?
A) One rak'ah with each group
B) Two rak'ahs with each group
C) One rak'ah with the first group and two with the second
D) The imam prays alone and the groups pray individually

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf allows Muslims to pray in congregation under threat by splitting into two groups, and any fighting during prayer invalidates it due to the principle of excessive action.

Salah — Prayer

Salat al-Khawf in Intense Fear: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling for prayer when fear is too intense for normal congregation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for Salat al-Khawf when fear is intense, identify its Quranic and Hadith proofs, and explain why gestures suffice for ruku' and sujud.

Core Idea
When fear prevents normal prayer, the obligation remains but the form reduces to gestures—the essence of prayer is preserved.

This lesson addresses the extreme scenario of Salat al-Khawf, when the normal congregational method is impossible. We learn that even in dire battle, salah is not abandoned; instead, the method is simplified. The Quranic verse and a companion saying provide the foundation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Salat al-Khawf when fear is intense. Ruling: fard 'ayn, but performed individually on foot or riding with gestures for ruku' and sujud.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and unanimous in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the first proof
Quran 2:239: 'And if you fear, then [pray] on foot or riding.' The verse shows that prayer is required even in fear, and the form can be simplified.
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fain khiftum' indicates obligation. The permission 'farijalan aw rukbanan' implies that normal bodily movements can be substituted when impossible.
This is the Hanafi principle of necessity (darura).
4
Locate the second proof
The saying of the Tabi'i Ibn Sirin regarding Salat al-Musayafah: 'He gestures with his head wherever his face is.'
This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and supports the practice.
5
Synthesize the ruling
The ruling is established by Quran and the practice of the Salaf. The usul principle is that necessity permits gestures, and the obligation remains intact.
No ikhtilaf is reported in the Hanafi school on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ اشْتَدَّ الْخَوْفُ صَلَّوْا رُكْبَانًا وُحْدَانًا يُومِئُونَ بِالرَّكُوعِ وَالسُّجُودِ وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَإِنْ اشْتَدَّ الْخَوْفُ صَلَّوْا رُكْبَانًا وُحْدَانًا {فَإِنْ خِفْتُمْ فَرِجَالًا أَوْ رُكْبَانًا فَإِذَا أَمِنتُمْ فَاذْكُرُوا اللَّهَ كَمَا عَلَّمَكُم مَّا لَمْ تَكُونُوا تَعْلَمُونَ}، (سورة البقرة، 4 الآية نمبر (239)
وجه:(۲) قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِنْ اشْتَدَّ الْخَوْفُ صَلَّوْا رُكْبَانًا وُحْدَانًا عَنِ ابْنِ سِيرِينَ، أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَقُولُ فِي صَلَاةِ الْمُسَايَفَةِ: «يُومِئُ إِيمَاءً حَيْثُ كَانَ وَجْهُهُ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه: في الصلاة عند المسايفة، نمبر 8267)
اصول: اگر معرکہ آرائی اس قدر شدید ہو کہ نماز کا وقت نہیں مل رہا ہے تو اپنی اپنی سواری پر ہی نماز پڑھ لے اور فان خفتم فرجالا اور كَهانا کی وجہ سے رکوع و سجدے کے لئے معذور ہو گا لہذا اشارے سے رکوع و سجدہ کرے۔
And if fear becomes intense, they pray riding/on foot individually, gesturing with bowing and prostration. Proof (1): The verse for establishing that if fear becomes intense, they pray riding/on foot individually: {And if you fear, then [pray] on foot or riding. And when you are safe, remember Allah as He has taught you that which you did not know.} (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:239) Proof (2): The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing that if fear becomes intense, they pray riding/on foot individually: from Ibn Sirin, he used to say in the prayer of sword-fighting: 'He gestures with his head wherever his face is.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: Regarding prayer during sword-fighting, number 8267). Principle: If the battle is so intense that there is no time for prayer, then one prays on his own mount, and because of the verse 'fain khiftum farijalan' and [the saying], one is excused from bowing and prostration, so he gestures with his head for ruku' and sujud.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This is a separate ruling for the situation when fear is so extreme that the normal two-group method of Salat al-Khawf is not feasible. In such a case, the obligation of prayer is not waived, but the method is simplified: each person prays individually, whether walking, running, or riding an animal. They do not need to face the qibla exactly and can perform ruku' and sujud by gestures (ima') with the head. The proof is from the Quranic verse 2:239, which explicitly permits prayer on foot or riding when in fear. Additionally, the saying of the Tabi'i Ibn Sirin confirms that during sword-fighting (musayafah), one gestures. The usul note explains that when battle prevents normal prayer, the individual is excused from bodily movements and uses gestures. This ruling is also from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is universally accepted by the Hanafi school; no ikhtilaf is mentioned.

Key Terms
إيماء (Ima'): Gesturing with the head or body instead of actual bowing and prostration when unable to perform them physically.
صلاة المسايفة (Salat al-Musayafah): Prayer performed during close combat or sword-fighting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for performing ruku' and sujud in Salat al-Khawf when fear is intense?
A) They are performed normally but quickly
B) They are omitted entirely
C) They are performed by gestures (ima')
D) They are made up later

Key Takeaway
In extreme fear, salah remains obligatory but is performed individually with gestures, as proven by Quran and practice.

Hadith Evidence for Salat al-Khawf
Provides two authentic hadith demonstrating the method of Salat al-Khawf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of Salat al-Khawf from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and Jabir, and explain how the Hanafi school reconciles the different rak'ah counts based on the imam's travel status.

Core Idea
Two authentic hadith show different rak'ah counts—Hanafi fiqh reconciles them by the imam's travel status.

In the previous lesson, we learned the rulings for Salat al-Khawf when the imam is a traveler or a resident. Now we turn to the primary textual evidence: two authentic hadith narrated by Ibn Mas'ud and Jabir that reveal the Prophet's practice. Understanding these hadith is essential to see how the Hanafi school derives its rulings from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two hadith sources.
Note the companion narrators (Ibn Mas'ud, Jabir) and the books (Abu Dawud, Muslim).
Both are ahad hadith, but considered authentic and relied upon.
2
Summarize the method in Ibn Mas'ud's hadith.
The Prophet prayed one rak'ah with the first group, then one rak'ah with the second group, then each group completed individually. Total for imam: 2 rak'ahs; each group: 2 rak'ahs.
This method applies when the imam is traveling and the prayer is shortened to 2 rak'ahs.
3
Summarize the method in Jabir's hadith.
The Prophet prayed two rak'ahs with the first group, then two rak'ahs with the second group. Total for imam: 4 rak'ahs; each group: 2 rak'ahs.
This method applies when the imam is a resident praying a 4-rak'ah prayer.
4
Reconcile the difference.
Hanafi scholars reconcile the two narrations by noting that the imam's state (traveler vs. resident) changes the total rak'ahs.
This reconciliation is supported by other hadith and the general principle of qasr al-salat.
5
Assess the evidentiary value.
Both hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but have strong sanad and matn. They are part of the Zahir al-Riwayah and used as primary evidence.
The Hanafi school does not require mutawatir evidence for practical rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ بْن مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: «صَلَّى بِنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلاةَ الخَوْفِ، فَقَامُوا صَفًّا خَلْفَ رَسُولِ اللهِ ، وَصَفٌ مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْعَدُوَّ ، فَصَلَّى بِهِمْ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم رَكْعَةً، ثُمَّ جَاءَ الْآخَرُونَ، فَقَامُوا مَقَامَهُمْ، وَاسْتَقْبَلَ هَؤُلَاءِ الْعَدُوَّ ، فَصَلَّى بِهِمُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم رَكْعَةً، ثُمَّ سَلَّمَ، فَقَامَ هَؤُلَاءِ، فَصَلَّوْا لِأَنْفُسِهِمْ رَكْعَةً، ثُمَّ سَلَّمُوا ، ثُمَّ ذَهَبُوا، فَقَامُوا مَقَامَ أُولَئِكَ مُسْتَقْبِلِي الْعَدُوِّ، وَرَجَعَ أُولَئِكَ إِلَى مَقَامِهِمْ، فَصَلَّوْا لِأَنْفُسِهِمْ رَكْعَةً، ثُمَّ سَلَّمُوا (سنن ابوداؤد باب من قال يصلي بكل طائفة ركعة ثم يسلم، نمبر 1244)
عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: « أَقْبَلْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم حَتَّى إِذَا كُنَّا بِذَاتِ الرِّقَاعِ قَالَ: كُنَّا إِذَا أَتَيْنَا عَلَى شَجَرَةٍ ظَلِيلَةٍ تَرَكْنَاهَا لِرَسُولِ اللهِ الله قَالَ : فَجَاءَ رَجُلٌ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ وَسَيْفُ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مُعَلَّقٌ بِشَجَرَةٍ فَأَخَذَ سَيْفَ نَبِيِّ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَاخْتَرَطَهُ، فَقَالَ لِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : أَتَخَافُنِي؟ قَالَ: لَا قَالَ: فَمَنْ يَمْنَعُكَ مِنِي؟ قَالَ: اللَّهُ يَمْنَعُنِي مِنْكَ. قَالَ: فَتَهَدَّدَهُ أَصْحَابُ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَأَغْمَدَ السَّيْفَ وَعَلَّقَهُ. قَالَ: فَنُودِيَ بِالصَّلَاةِ فَصَلَّى بِطَائِفَةٍ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ تَأخَرُوا وَصَلَّى بِالطَّائِفَةِ الْأُخْرَى رَكْعَتَيْنِ. قَالَ: فَكَانَتْ لِرَسُولِ اللهِ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أَرْبَعُ رَكَعَاتٍ وَلِلْقَوْمِ رَكْعَتَانِ » (مسلم شريف: باب صلاة الخوف، نمبر 843 سنن ابوداؤد باب من قال يصلي بكل طائفة ركعتين، نمبر 1248)
From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah led us in the prayer of fear. They stood in a row behind the Messenger of Allah, and another row facing the enemy. The Messenger of Allah led them in one rak'ah, then the others came and took their place, and these ones faced the enemy. The Prophet led them in one rak'ah, then he said salam. Then these ones stood and prayed one rak'ah for themselves, then said salam. Then they went and stood in the place of those, facing the enemy, and those others returned to their place and prayed one rak'ah for themselves, then said salam.' (Sunan Abu Dawud: Chapter of who says he prays with each group one rak'ah then says salam, number 1244) From Jabir, he said: 'We came with the Messenger of Allah until we were at Dhat al-Riqa'. He said: We used to leave a shady tree for the Messenger of Allah. A man from the polytheists came and took the sword of the Prophet, which was hanging on a tree, and drew it. He said to the Messenger of Allah: Do you fear me? He said: No. He said: Who will protect you from me? He said: Allah will protect me from you. The Companions threatened him, so he sheathed the sword and hung it. Then the call to prayer was made, and he prayed with one group two rak'ahs, then they stepped back and he prayed with the other group two rak'ahs. So the Messenger of Allah had four rak'ahs and the people had two.' (Muslim: Chapter of the Prayer of Fear, number 843; Sunan Abu Dawud: Chapter of who says he prays with each group two rak'ahs, number 1248)
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents two authentic hadith that serve as direct evidence for the method of Salat al-Khawf described in the previous lessons. The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud demonstrates the method where the imam prays one rak'ah with each group for a two-rak'ah prayer, and each group completes their second rak'ah individually. This matches the first ruling in Lesson 1. The hadith of Jabir shows another legitimate method where the imam (who was traveling? Actually, the hadith context: the Prophet was a resident? He prayed two rak'ahs with each group, totaling four for himself, and each group got two rak'ahs. This corresponds to the case when the imam is a resident (muqim) as mentioned in the earlier ruling: 'if the imam is a resident, he prays with the first group two rak'ahs and with the second two rak'ahs.' Both hadith are from authentic sources (Abu Dawud, Muslim) and are used by the Hanafi school to justify both scenarios. The author includes these here as additional textual proofs. Note that there is a slight discrepancy: the Jabir hadith mentions the imam praying four rak'ahs total, which is consistent with the resident imam. These hadith are part of the Zahir al-Riwayah canon and are considered strong evidence.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): The method used by the Prophet during battle as narrated in these hadith.
مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْعَدُوِّ (Mustaqbil al-'Aduw): Facing the enemy direction to maintain guard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, how many rak'ahs did the Prophet pray with the first group before they faced the enemy?
A) One rak'ah
B) Two rak'ahs
C) He prayed the entire prayer alone
D) He did not pray until after battle

Key Takeaway
The two authentic hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and Jabir provide the evidence for the two methods of Salat al-Khawf, reconciled by the imam's travel status.

Rulings on Shrouding the Deceased (Takfin)
Quduri matn on shrouding rules with supporting hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah practices of shrouding a deceased Muslim and identify which actions are prohibited or recommended based on the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Shrouding in three garments is sunnah, not fard; cutting nails or combing hair is prohibited.

This lesson covers the key rulings on takfin (shrouding) as presented by Imam al-Quduri. You will learn the standard practice for men and women, the actions that are recommended (sunnah) such as perfuming the shroud in odd numbers, and those that are prohibited, like combing the hair or cutting nails. The evidence from hadith and the practice of the Companions and Tabi'un is also discussed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic rulings
Read the passage and note the hukm (ruling) for each action: what is permissible (ja'iz), what is sunnah, and what is prohibited (haram).
2
Distinguish fard kifayah from sunnah
Understand that the obligation to shroud is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), but the specific number of garments and details are sunnah muakkadah.
3
List the prohibited actions
Identify the actions that are explicitly forbidden: combing the hair or beard of the deceased, and cutting nails or hair. These are based on the principle that the deceased is not to be treated as a living person.
4
Analyze the evidence
Examine the hadith and statements of the Tabi'un that support each ruling, such as the hadith on tajmir with odd numbers and the narration from Umm Atiyyah about braiding the hair.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصل فِي التَّكْفِيْنِ فَإِنْ اقْتَصَرُوا عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَثْوَابِ جَازَ وَيَكُون الْخِمَارُ فَوْقَ الْقَمِيصِ تَحْتَ اللِّفَافَةِ . وَيُجْعَلُ شَعْرُهَا عَلَى صَدْرِهَا وَلَا يُسَرَّحُ شَعْرُ الْمَيِّتِ وَلَا لِحْيَتُهُ وَلَا يُقَصُّ ظُفْرُهُ وَلَا شَعْرُهُ وَتُجَمَّرُ الْأَكْفَانُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُدْرَجَ فِيهَا وِتْرًا فَإِنْ خَافُوا أَنْ تَنْتَشِرَ الْأَكْفَانُ عَنْهُ عَقَدُوهَا فَإِذَا فَرَغُوا مِنْهُ صَلَّوْا عَلَيْهِ الْمَرْأَةُ الَّتِي حَاضَتْ فِي خَمْسَةِ أَثْوَابِ أَوْ ثَلَاثَةٍ (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه: ما قالوا في كم تكفن المرأة، نمبر 11085)
وجه (۴) قول التابعي لثبوت وَتُكَفَّنُ الْمَرْأَةُ فِي خَمْسَةِ أَثْوَابِ عَنِ ابْنِ سِيرِينَ، قَالَ: «تُوضَعُ الْخُرْقَةُ عَلَى بَطْنِهَا ، وَتُعَصِبُ بِمَا فَخِذَيْهَا» (مصنف ابن شيبه في الخرقة أين توضع في المرأة، 11092)
وجه:(۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَيَكُون الْخِمَارُ فَوْقَ الْقَمِيصِ تَحْتَ اللِّفَافَةِ \ سَأَلْتُ أَمُّ الْهُدَيْلِ ابْنَةَ سِيرِينَ، هَلْ رَأَيْتُ حَفْصَةَ إِذَا غَسَلَتْ كَيْفَ تَصْنَعُ بِخِمَارِ الْمَرْأَةِ؟ قَالَتْ: «نَعَمْ، كَانَتْ تُخَمِّرُهَا كَمَا تُخَمَّرُ الْحَيَّةُ، ثُمَّ يَفْضُلُ مِنَ الْخِمَارِ قَدْرُ ذِرَاعٍ، فَتَفْرِشُهُ فِي مُؤَخِّرِهَا، ثُمَّ تَعْطِفُ تِلْكَ الْفَضْلَةَ، فَتُغَطِي بِمَا وَجْهَهَا» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في المرأة كيف تخمر، نمبر 11107)
د وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيُجْعَلُ شَعْرُهَا عَلَى صَدْرِهَا وَلَا يُسَرَّحُ \ عَنْ أُمِّ عَطِيَّةَ قَالَتْ: «وَضَفَّرْنَا رَأْسَهَا ثَلَاثَةَ قُرُونٍ ثُمَّ أَلْقَيْنَاهَا خَلْفَهَا مُقَدَّمَ رَأْسِهَا وَقَرْنَيْهَا» (سنن ابوداؤد: باب كيف غسل الميت نمبر 3144 بخاری شریف: باب يلقى شعر المرأة خلفها، نمبر 1263)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيُجْعَلُ شَعْرُهَا عَلَى صَدْرِهَا وَلَا يُسَرَّحُ \ أَنَّ عَائِشَةَ رَأَتِ امْرَأَةً يَكُدُّونَ رَأْسَهَا، فَقَالَتْ : عَلَامَ تَنْصُونَ مَيْتَكُمْ (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، بَابُ شَعْرِ الْمَيِّتِ وَأَطْفَارِهِ، نمبر 6232)
د وجه (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَلَا يُقَصُّ ظُفْرُهُ وَلَا شَعْرُهُ \ سُئِلَ حَمَّادٌ، عَنْ تَقْلِيمٍ أَطْفَارِ الْمَيِّتِ؟ قَالَ: «أَرَأَيْتَ إِنْ كَانَ أَقْلَفَ أَتَكْتِنُهُ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ شَعْرِ الْمَيِّتِ وأَظفاره، نمبر 6233)
كوجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَتُجَمَّرُ الْأَكْفَانُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُدْرَجَ فِيهَا وِتْرًا أَعَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : " إِذَا أَجْمَرْتُمُ الْمَيِّتَ فَأَوْتِرُوا " وَرُوِي " أَجْمِرُوا كَفَنَ الْمَيِّتِ ثَلَاثًا " (سنن بيهقي: باب الحنوط للميت، نمبر 6702 مصنف ابن ابي شيبه من قال يكون تجمر ثيابه وترا، نمبر 11113)
اصول : عذر کی بناء پر مرد کو دو کپڑوں میں کفن دینا بھی جائز ہے ایک ازار اور دوسرے لفافہ ۔
Section on shrouding: If they limit to three garments, it is permissible. The khimar (headcover) should be above the qamis (shirt) under the lifafah (wrapper). Her hair should be placed on her chest, and the hair of the deceased should not be combed, nor his beard, nor should his nails or hair be cut. The shrouds should be perfumed with incense before wrapping them, in odd number. If they fear the shrouds will fall off, they may tie them. When they finish, they pray over him. The woman who has menstruated (i.e., adult woman) is shrouded in five garments or three. (Ibn Abi Shaybah: 11085) Wajh 4: Saying of a Tabi'i for confirmation: The woman is shrouded in five garments according to Ibn Sirin: 'The piece of cloth is placed on her belly, and she is bound with it on her thighs.' (11092) Wajh 1: Saying of a Tabi'i: The khimar is above the qamis under the lifafah: I asked Umm al-Hudhayl bint Sirin: 'Did you see Hafsa when she washed, how did she place the woman's khimar?' She said: 'Yes, she would cover her as a living woman covers herself, then there would be an extra cubit from the khimar, which she would spread behind her, then she would fold that extra piece and cover her face with it.' (11107) Wajh 1: Hadith: Her hair is placed on her chest and not combed: From Umm Atiyyah: 'We braided her hair into three strands, then we threw them behind her: front of her head and its two sides.' (Abu Dawud 3144, Bukhari 1263) Wajh 2: Hadith: Aisha saw a woman whose hair was being combed and said: 'Why do you harm your deceased?' (Abd al-Razzaq 6232) Wajh 1: Saying of a Tabi'i: His nails should not be cut nor his hair: Hammad was asked about trimming the deceased's nails; he said: 'Do you think if he was uncircumcised, would you circumcise him?' (Abd al-Razzaq 6233) K-wajh 1: Hadith: The shrouds are perfumed with incense before wrapping them in odd number: From Jabir: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When you perfume the deceased, perfume with odd numbers.' And it is reported: 'Perfume the shroud of the deceased three times.' (Bayhaqi 6702, Ibn Abi Shaybah 11113) Principle: Due to necessity, it is also permissible to shroud a man in two garments: one izaar (wrapper) and the other lifafah.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri presents the rulings on shrouding the deceased (takfin). It begins by stating the standard practice: three garments are sufficient for a man: the izaar (lower wrapper), qamis (shirt), and lifafah (overall wrapper). The khimar (headcover) is placed above the qamis but under the lifafah. For a woman, her hair is placed on her chest, and it is prohibited to comb the hair or beard of the deceased, or to cut the nails or hair. The shrouds should be perfumed with incense (tajmir) an odd number of times before wrapping. If there is fear that the shrouds will come undone, they may be tied. After shrouding, the funeral prayer is performed. An adult woman (who has menstruated) is shrouded in five garments or three. The text then supports each ruling with evidence: the practice of the Companions and Tabi'un, and hadith. For example, the hadith of Umm Atiyyah shows that the hair of a deceased woman is braided and placed behind her, not combed. The prohibition of cutting nails and hair is based on a statement of Hammad: if circumcision is not done after death, neither should these acts. The tajmir is supported by the Prophet's command to use odd numbers. The passage also notes a principle: due to necessity (e.g., shortage of cloth), a man may be shrouded in just two garments (izaar and lifafah), indicating leniency. Overall, these rulings are sunnah (recommended) and not obligatory, as the text says 'jaaz' (permissible) for the basic three, implying that fewer may also be acceptable in hardship.

Key Terms
تكفين (takfin): The act of shrouding the deceased in burial garments.
خمار (khimar): A headcover used as part of the shroud for women, placed above the qamis and under the lifafah.
تجمير (tajmir): Perfuming the shroud with incense (bakhoor) before wrapping the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Quduri, what is the ruling on combing the hair or cutting the nails of the deceased?
A) It is required (wajib)
B) It is prohibited (haram)
C) It is allowed (mubah) but not recommended
D) It is recommended (sunnah) only for women

Key Takeaway
Shrouding the deceased in three garments for men and five for women is a highly recommended sunnah, not an obligation, and certain actions like combing hair or cutting nails are prohibited.

Who Leads the Janazah Prayer: The Hanafi Hierarchy
Ruling on precedence in leading funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead the janazah prayer and explain the ruling on the wali repeating the prayer.

Core Idea
The sultan leads, then the imam, then the wali; if another leads, the wali should repeat.

The funeral prayer is a communal obligation, but who should lead it? The Hanafi school establishes a clear order of precedence to avoid conflict and honor authority. This lesson examines the ruling from al-Quduri and the proofs that support it, including a cross-madhhab comparison.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling type
The act is the prayer over the deceased (janazah). The ruling on who leads is a sunnah/mustahabb preference, not obligatory. Determine the hukm level from the text.
The prayer itself is fard kifayah; the leadership order is mustahabb.
2
Extract the hierarchy
From the text: the most entitled is the sultan (ruler), if present; if not, the imam of the locality, then the wali. Note the condition: only if the sultan is absent does the imam take precedence.
The Urdu notes add: the judge of the city comes before the locality imam.
3
Analyze the wali's repetition rule
If someone other than the sultan or wali leads, the wali should repeat the prayer. This restores the wali's right. However, if the wali leads himself, no one may repeat after him.
Repetition is mustahabb, not fard.
4
Examine the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn about the Prophet praying over the Najashi. The Prophet acted as sultan, establishing his precedence. Also, athar from Umar and Hasan support the wali's right.
The Hanafi position uses the hadith to prioritize the ruler's public authority.
5
Contrast with Shafi'i view
The Shafi'i school gives the wali the primary right, based on the hadith 'al-wali ahaqq'. Understand how the Hanafi school reconciles this by considering the sultan as the general wali.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; both positions are well-founded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الصلوة علي الميت
وَأَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِالصَّلَاةِ عَلَيْهِ السُّلْطَانُ إِذَا حَضَرَ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَحْضُرُ فَيُسْتَحَبُّ تَقْدِيمُ إمَامِ الْحَيَ ثُمَّ الْوَلِيُّ وَإِنْ صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُ الْوَلِي أَوْ السُّلْطَانِ أَعَادَ الْوَلِيُّ الصَّلَاةَ وَإِنْ صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ الْوَلِيُّ لَمْ يَجْزْ أَنْ يُصَلِّيَ أَحَدٌ بَعْدَهُ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَأَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِالصَّلَاةِ عَلَيْهِ السُّلْطَانُ \ عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ قَالَ: قَالَ لَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إِنَّ أَخَاكُمُ النَّجَاشِيَّ قَدْ مَاتَ فَقُومُوا فَصَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ»، قَالَ: فَقُمْنَا، فَصَفَفْنَا كَمَا يُصَفُ عَلَى المَيِّتِ، وَصَلَّيْنَا عَلَيْهِ كَمَا يُصَلَّى عَلَى المَيِّتِ (سنن ترمذي: باب ما جاء في صلاة النبي على النجاشي، 1039 بخاري شريف: الصلاة على الجنائز بالمصلى 1327)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَأَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِالصَّلَاةِ عَلَيْهِ السُّلْطَانُ \ عَنْ عَلِقٍ، قَالَ: «الْإِمَامُ أَحَقُّ مَنْ صَلَّى عَلَى جِنَازَةٍ ذَهَبْتُ مَعَ إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِلَى جِنَازَةٍ وَهُوَ وَلِيُّهَا، «فَأَرْسَلَ إِلَى إِمَامِ الْحَيَ فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهَا» (مصنف ابن شيبه : ما قالوا في تقدم الإمام على الجنازة،نمبر11306,11305)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَأَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِالصَّلَاةِ عَلَيْهِ السُّلْطَانُ اعَنْ عُمَرَ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «الْوَلِيُّ أَحَقُّ بِالصَّلَاةِ عَلَيْهَا» (مصنف عبدالرزاق باب من أحق بالصلاة على الميت،نمبر 6373)
وجه (۴) قول التابعي لثبوت وَأَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِالصَّلَاةِ عَلَيْهِ السُّلْطَانُ \ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: «أَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِالصَّلَاةِ عَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ الْأَبُ ثُمَّ الزَّوْجُ ، ثُمَّ الإِبْنُ ثُمَّ الْأَخُ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق: بَابُ مَنْ أَحَقُّ بِالصَّلَاةِ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ، نمبر 6370)
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُ الْوَلِي أَوْ السُّلْطَانِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ : «أَنَّ أَسْوَدَ رَجُلًا أَوِ امْرَأَةً، كَانَ يَقُمُ الْمَسْجِدَ فَمَاتَ وَلَمْ يَعْلَمْ بِمَوْتِهِ، فَذَكَرَهُ ذَاتَ يَوْمٍ فَقَالَ: مَا فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ الْإِنْسَانُ؟ قَالُوا: مَاتَ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ، قَالَ: أَفَلَا آذَنْتُمُونِي؟ فَقَالُوا: إِنَّهُ كَانَ كَذَا وَكَذَا قِصَّتُهُ. قَالَ: فَحَقَرُوا شَأْنَهُ قَالَ: فَدُلُّوي عَلَى قَبْرِهِ. فَأَتَى قَبْرَهُ فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ.» (بخاري شريف: باب الصلاة على القبر بعدما يدفن، سنن ابوداؤد: باب الصلاة على القبر،نمبر 3203)
اصول: نماز جنازہ فرض کفایہ ہے یعنی اگر کچھ لوگ بھی ادا کر لیں تو فرض ادا ہو جائے گا۔
اصول: نماز جنازہ پڑھانے کا زیادہ حق بادشاہ کا ہے پھر قاضی شہر پھر محلہ کا امام پھر میت کاولی۔
Section on the funeral prayer. The most entitled of people to pray over him is the ruler (sultan) if present. If he is not present, then it is recommended to present the imam of the locality, then the wali (guardian/relative). If someone other than the wali or ruler prays over him, the wali should repeat the prayer. If the wali prayed, it is not permissible for anyone to pray after him. (Proofs follows: Hadith of Imran ibn Husayn about the Najashi, saying of Alqamah, hadith of Umar, saying of Hasan, hadith of Abu Hurayra about the black man who cleaned the mosque) Principles: Funeral prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah): if some people perform it, the obligation is discharged. Principle: The one with the most right to lead the funeral prayer is the king, then the judge of the city, then the imam of the locality, then the wali of the deceased.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage addresses the hierarchy of who should lead the funeral prayer (imam in janazah). The ruling is that the most entitled person is the ruler (sultan) if present, because he represents the public authority. If the ruler is not present, it is recommended (mustahabb) to present the imam of the locality, and then the wali (the closest relative, such as the father, son, or brother). The text then addresses a scenario: if someone other than the wali or ruler leads the prayer, the wali should repeat the prayer, meaning he should lead a second congregation if possible, because the wali's right is not waived by the unauthorized person. However, if the wali himself led the prayer, no one else may pray after him, as the prayer is already valid and one congregation is sufficient. The supporting evidence includes several hadith and athar: the Prophet led the prayer over the Najashi (an absent ruler) indicating the ruler's precedence, the practice of Ibrahim (al-Nakha'i) deferring to the local imam, and the statement of Umar that the wali is more entitled. The hadith of Abu Hurayra about the Prophet praying over the black man at the grave shows that even if the rightful person did not lead, the prayer can be valid, but the repetition by the wali is recommended to restore the proper order. The Urdu notes add that funeral prayer is fard kifayah (communal obligation) and clarify the hierarchy: king, city judge, locality imam, then wali.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): The guardian or closest male relative of the deceased (e.g., father, son, brother) who is entitled to lead the funeral prayer or choose the imam.
سلطان (sultan): The political ruler or head of state, who has the highest right to lead the funeral prayer as the representative of the community.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation: if some Muslims perform it, the obligation is lifted from all; if none perform it, all sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Quduri, what should the wali do if someone other than the wali or sultan has led the funeral prayer?
A) The wali should not pray at all
B) The wali should repeat the prayer (i.e., lead another congregation)
C) The wali should criticize the person but accept the prayer as valid
D) The wali should pray alone at the grave later

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the sultan leads the janazah prayer; if the sultan is absent, the imam of the locality leads, then the wali; the wali should repeat if someone else led without his right.

Performing Janazah Prayer at the Grave
Ruling with proofs for janazah prayer at grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing janazah prayer at the grave, identify the condition under which it is allowed, and cite the supporting proofs from the source.

Core Idea
Prayer at the grave is allowed only if missed before burial; repeating it is prohibited.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in funeral rites: a deceased person has been buried without the janazah prayer. According to the Hanafi school, it is recommended to perform the prayer at the grave, but only on the condition that the prayer was not already performed before burial. The commentator provides three pieces of evidence, including the practice of the Companions and the Prophet himself, and adds a crucial qualification to prevent repetition.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its condition
Identify the hukm (permissible, sunnah) and the explicit condition: the janazah prayer was not performed before burial.
The third proof explicitly forbids repeating the prayer.
2
Identify the first proof: practice of Ibn Umar
Recognize the action of Ibn Umar as evidence from a Companion (qawl al-sahabi). He prayed at the grave of his brother Asim after returning from a journey.
3
Identify the second proof: action of the Prophet
Recognize the hadith of al-Bara' ibn Ma'rur: the Prophet prayed over him after burial. This is a direct prophetic action (fi'l).
This is the primary dalil used by the Hanafis.
4
Identify the third proof: qualification
Note the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'The deceased is not prayed over twice.' This establishes that the ruling only applies when the prayer was missed.
This serves as a condition that limits the scope of the previous proofs.
5
Understand the cross-madhhab dispute
Recognize that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not permit prayer at the grave after burial at all, considering it an innovation.
The Hanafi position is based on the prophetic action; the Shafi'i position considers it an abrogated or unique case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ دُفِنَ وَلَمْ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِ صَلَّى عَلَى قَبْرِهِ. وجه : (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت فَإِنْ دُفِنَ وَلَمْ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِ صَلَّى عَلَى قَبْرِهِ \ تُوُفِّيَ عَاصِمُ بْنُ عُمَرَ وَابْنُ عُمَرَ غَائِبٌ فَقَدِمَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ قَالَ: أَيُّوبُ، أَحْسَبُهُ قَالَ بِثَلَاثٍ، قَالَ: فَقَالَ: «أَرُونِي قَبْرَ أَخِي»، فَأَرُوهُ فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في الميت يصلى عليه بعدما دفن من فعله، نمبر 11940 سنن بيهقي : باب الصلاة على القبر بعدما يدفن الميت،نمبر 7025) وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ دُفِنَ وَلَمْ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِ صَلَّى عَلَى قَبْرِهِ \ «أَنَّ الْبَرَاءَ بْنَ مَعْرُورٍ، تُوُفِّيَ فِي صَفَرٍ قَبْلَ قُدُومِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمَدِينَةَ بِشَهْرٍ، فَلَمَّا قَدِمَ صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه: فِي الْمَيِّتِ يُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ بَعْدَمَا دُفِنَ مَنْ فَعَلَهُ ، نمبر 11933/السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى الْقَبْرِ بَعْدَمَا يُدْفَنُ الْمَيِّتُ، نمبر 7021) وجه:(۳) قول التابعي لثبوت فَإِنْ دُفِنَ وَلَمْ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِ صَلَّى عَلَى قَبْرِهِ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «لَا يُصَلَّى عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ مَرَّتَيْنِ» مصنف ابن ابي شيبه من كان لا يرى الصلاة عليها إذا دفنت وقد صلي عليها، غير 11946)
If he is buried and no prayer was performed over him, then prayer is performed over his grave. Evidence: (1) Statement of a follower (tabi'i) to establish this: 'Asim ibn Umar died and Ibn Umar was absent; he came after that. Ayyub said: I think he said after three (days). He said: Show me my brother's grave. So they showed him and he prayed over him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the deceased prayed over after burial, #11940; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on prayer over the grave after the deceased is buried, #7025) Evidence: (2) The hadith to establish this: 'Al-Bara' ibn Ma'rur died in Safar one month before the arrival of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to Madinah. When he arrived, he prayed over him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: On the deceased prayed over after burial, #11933; Sunan al-Kubra al-Bayhaqi, #7021) Evidence: (3) Statement of a follower to establish this: From Ibrahim who said: 'The deceased is not prayed over twice.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on those who did not consider prayer upon the deceased if buried and already prayed over, #11946)
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Al-Quduri presents a ruling: if a deceased person is buried without the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah), then the prayer should be performed at the grave. The commentary then provides three pieces of evidence. The first is the practice of Ibn Umar, who prayed at the grave of his brother Asim after returning from a journey. The second is the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who, after arriving in Madinah, performed the funeral prayer over Al-Bara' ibn Ma'rur who had died and been buried before the Prophet's arrival. The third evidence, from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, states that the deceased should not be prayed over twice. This is a qualification: the ruling applies only if the prayer was not performed before burial; if it was already performed, then it is not repeated at the grave. This condition is important in practice: one must ascertain that the janazah prayer was indeed missed.

Key Terms
دُفِنَ (dufina): He was buried; past tense passive verb indicating the deceased has been interred.
صَلَّى عَلَى قَبْرِهِ (salla 'ala qabrihi): Performed the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) at the grave of the deceased.
ثبوت (thubut): Establishment or proof; the evidence that confirms the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is it permissible to perform the janazah prayer at the grave according to this passage?
A) If the deceased was a man
B) If the deceased was a woman
C) If the funeral prayer was not performed before burial
D) If more than one person is present

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits janazah prayer at the grave only if it was missed before burial; repeating it is prohibited.

Position of the Imam at the Chest During Janazah
Ruling and proofs for the imam standing at the chest of the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where the imam stands during janazah prayer for a male and female deceased, and cite the proofs from the tabi'een.

Core Idea
The Hanafi imam stands at the chest for a man and at the shoulder for a woman—a sunnah based on the practice of the early tabi'een.

In the funeral prayer (janazah), the position of the imam relative to the deceased is a matter of established practice. The Hanafi school holds a specific position—at the chest for a man and at the shoulder for a woman—supported by the actions and statements of the companions and their followers. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs, helping you understand the gender-based distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The matn states that the person praying stands in line with the chest of the deceased. Determine the hukm level: this is a recommended practice (sunnah muakkadah), not obligatory.
2
Locate the Dalil
Two proofs are cited: (1) the statement of Ata' ibn Abi Rabah that the imam stands at the chest, and (2) the practice of Anas ibn Malik who stood at the head of the deceased (near the chest). Identify these as transmitted reports from the tabi'een and a companion.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Ata's statement directly commands the position at the chest. Anas's action shows the established practice of standing near the head/chest. The Hanafi school uses these as evidence for the sunnah position.
Anas stood at the head, but the Hanafi school interprets 'at the head' as equivalent to chest-level for a male.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that the imam stands at the head for a man and at the middle for a woman. Understand the basis of their difference.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: if an imam stands at the head for a man (unlike the Hanafi chest position), the prayer is still valid but the sunnah is missed. This does not invalidate the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقوم المصلي بحذاء صدرالميت. وجه:(۱) قول التابعي لثبوت ويقوم المصلي بحذاء صدرالميت \ عَنْ عَطَاءٍ، قَالَ: «إِذَا صَلَّى الرَّجُلُ عَلَى الْجِنَازَةِ قَامَ عِنْدَ الصَّدْرِ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في المرأة أين يقام منها في الصلاة والرجل أين يقام منه، نمبر 11551 مصنف عبدالرزاق باب أين يقوم الإمام من الجنازة، نمبر 6352) وجه : (۲) قول التابعي لثبوت ويقوم المصلي بحذاء صدرالميت \ قَالُوا: هَذَا أَنَسُ بْنُ مَالِكٍ ، فَلَمَّا وُضِعَتِ الْجِنَازَةُ قَامَ أَنَسٌ فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهَا وَأَنَا خَلْفَهُ لَا يَحُولُ بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَهُ شَيْءٌ فَقَامَ عِنْدَ رَأْسِهِ فَكَبَّرَ أَرْبَعَ تَكْبِيرَاتٍ لَمْ يُطِلْ وَلَمْ يُسْرِعْ ثُمَّ ذَهَبَ يَقْعُدُ فَقَالُوا: يَا أَبَا حَمْزَةَ الْمَرْأَةُ الْأَنْصَارِيَّةُ فَقَرَّبُوهَا
The one praying stands in line with the chest of the deceased. Evidence: (1) Statement of a follower to establish this: from Ata' who said: 'When a man prays over the funeral, he stands at the chest.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on where to stand for a woman and where to stand for a man in prayer, #11551; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on where the imam stands for the funeral, #6352) Evidence: (2) Statement of a follower to establish this: They said: 'This is Anas ibn Malik. When the funeral was placed, Anas stood and prayed over it while I was behind him with nothing between us; he stood at its head and said four takbirs, neither lengthy nor quick, then he went to sit. They said: O Abu Hamzah, the Ansari woman. So they brought her forward.'
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the proper position of the person leading the janazah prayer. The matn states that the imam stands in line with the chest of the deceased. The commentary offers two proofs from the tabi'een (followers). First, the statement of Ata' ibn Abi Rabahdirectly states that when a man prays over a funeral, he stands at the chest. Second, the actual practice of Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) is narrated: when he led the janazah prayer for a man, he stood at the head (which is near the chest area). Note that in the Hanafi school, the imam stands at the chest of a male deceased and at the shoulder of a female deceased. This passage only discusses the male case.

Key Terms
بحذاء صدر الميت (bihidha'i sadri al-mayyit): In line with the chest of the deceased; where the imam stands during the funeral prayer.
الجنازة (al-janazah): The funeral bier or the funeral prayer itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, where does the imam stand when praying over a male deceased?
A) At the head
B) At the feet
C) In line with the chest
D) At the side

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the imam stands at the chest for a male and at the shoulder for a female deceased during the janazah prayer, based on the practice of the early Muslims.

Procedure of the Janazah Prayer: Four Takbirs
Summary of the steps of the funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four takbirs of the janazah prayer and identify which recitation follows each takbir according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The janazah prayer is four takbirs: after each, a specific sunnah recitation — thana, darood, dua, then salam.

The funeral prayer is a communal obligation with a unique structure. Unlike the five daily prayers, it has no bowing or prostration. Instead, it consists of four consecutive takbirs (saying 'Allahu Akbar'), each followed by a silent recitation. This passage from the Hanafi text summarizes the procedure clearly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four takbirs
The janazah prayer has four distinct takbirs. Each takbir marks a step in the prayer, similar to the units in regular salah.
The takbirs themselves are wajib in the Hanafi school.
2
Associate recitations with each takbir
After the first takbir, recite thana (Subhanakallahumma...). After the second, recite darood (salutations upon the Prophet). After the third, make dua for the deceased. After the fourth, say salam.
These recitations are sunnah, not wajib.
3
Understand the legal status
In the Hanafi school, the four takbirs and the salam are wajib. The recitations (thana, darood, dua) are sunnah. Missing a takbir intentionally invalidates the prayer; unintentional omission requires repetition.
This distinction is key for validity.
4
Contrast with other schools
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require recitation of Surat al-Fatihah after the first takbir. Hanafis do not, relying on the practice of the Companions and the established sunnah.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فِي الصَّلوةِ عَلي الحَيَّتِ اصول: نماز جنازہ کی پہلی تکبیر میں ثنا، دوسری میں درود ، تیسری میں میت کے لئے دعاء، اور چوتھی میں سلام پھیر دیا جائے، بس یہ مکمل نماز جنازہ ہے۔
On the prayer over the deceased. Principle: In the first takbir of the funeral prayer, the thana (glorification) is recited; in the second, the darood (salutations upon the Prophet); in the third, supplication for the deceased; and in the fourth, the salam is given. That is the complete funeral prayer.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage from the Urdu commentary outlines the standard procedure of the janazah prayer according to the Hanafi school. It states that the prayer consists of four takbirs. After the first takbir, the thana (subhanakallahumma) is recited silently. After the second takbir, the darood (salawat upon the Prophet, peace be upon him) is recited. After the third takbir, one makes supplication (dua) for the deceased, typically the standard janazah dua. After the fourth takbir, the salam is given to both sides. This is the complete method. Note that recitation of thana, darood, and dua is sunnah; the takbirs themselves are wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'; each is a distinct step in the janazah prayer.
ثنا (thana): The glorification said after the first takbir, typically 'Subhanakallahumma...'
درود (darood): The salutation upon the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), e.g., 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is recited after the second takbir in the janazah prayer according to the passage?
A) Thana
B) Darood
C) Dua for the deceased
D) Salam

Key Takeaway
The janazah prayer consists of four takbirs; the recitations after each are sunnah, while the takbirs themselves and the salam are wajib.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on Salat al-Janazah: Takbirs, Recitations, and Prohibition of Mosque Prayer
Comprehensive coverage of janazah prayer rulings from matn and commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four takbirs and their associated recitations in janazah prayer, and explain the Hanafi ruling that praying janazah in a mosque is makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Janazah prayer is four takbirs with specific supplications; praying it in a mosque is makruh tanzihi in the Hanafi school.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn, accompanied by extensive commentary and proofs, lays out the essential structure of the funeral prayer. It specifies what is said after each of the four takbirs, addresses a key disagreement with the Shafi'i school, and establishes an important ruling about where the prayer should be performed. Understanding these details ensures the prayer is performed correctly in accordance with the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its components
Janazah prayer consists of four takbirs. At each takbir, a specific recitation is made: praise of Allah after the first, blessings on the Prophet after the second, du'a for the deceased and Muslims after the third, and taslim after the fourth. Note the sequence and that hands are raised only in the first takbir.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of the Prophet praying four takbirs over an-Najashi (Bukhari) is the main proof for the number of takbirs. Also noted are the practice of the Prophet standing at the middle of a woman and the du'a narrated by Abu Hurairah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit action of the Prophet shows that four takbirs are the established practice. Hanafis consider this wajib because the Prophet consistently did it. The specific recitations are sunnah but the takbirs are essential.
4
Analyze the madhhab dispute on mosque prayer
The passage presents evidence from both Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding praying janazah inside a mosque. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh tanzihi; the Shafi'i position is that it is permissible. Note the opposing evidence and the Hanafi response.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi response interprets the hadith 'Whoever prays over a janazah in the mosque, nothing is upon him' as meaning no sin, but the act is still makruh due to other prohibitions. The incident of Suhayl ibn Bayda is considered abrogated or specific. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Hanafi view of karahah.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فِي الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى الْجِنَازَةِ. وَالصَّلَاةُ أَنْ يُكَبِّرَ تَكْبِيرَةً يَحْمَدُ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى عَقِيبَهَا ثُمَّ يُكَبِّرُ تَكْبِيرَةً ثَانِيَةً وَيُصَلِّي عَلَى النَّبِيِّ - صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ - وَعَلَيْهَا نَعْشٌ أَخْضَرُ فَقَامَ عِنْدَ عَجِيزَتِهَا، فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهَا نَحْوَ صَلَاتِهِ عَلَى الرَّجُلِ، ثُمَّ جَلَسَ فَقَالَ الْعَلَاءُ بْنُ زِيَادٍ: يَا أَبَا حَمْزَةَ هَكَذَا كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُصَلِّي عَلَى الْجِنَازَةِ كَصَلَاتِكَ، يُكَبِّرُ عَلَيْهَا أَرْبَعًا، وَيَقُومُ عِنْدَ رَأْسِ الرَّجُلِ وَعَجِيزَةِ الْمَرْأَةِ؟ قَالَ: نَعَمْ (سنن أبي داود: باب أين يقوم الإمام من الميت إذا صلى عليه، رقم 3194) وَجْهٌ: (3) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِنْ دُفِنَ وَلَمْ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِ صَلَّى عَلَى قَبْرِهِ \ حَدَّثَنَا سَمُرَةُ بْنُ جُنْدُبٍ قَالَ: «صَلَّيْتُ وَرَاءَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَلَى امْرَأَةٍ مَاتَتْ فِي نِفَاسِهَا، فَقَامَ عَلَيْهَا وَسَطَهَا.» (البخاري: باب أين يقوم من المرأة والرجل، رقم 1332، مسلم: باب أين يقوم الإمام من الميت للصلاة عليه، رقم 964، سنن أبي داود: باب أين يقوم الإمام من الميت إذا صلى عليه، رقم 3195) وَوَجْهُ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالصَّلَاةُ أَنْ يُكَبِّرَ تَكْبِيرَةً يَحْمَدُ اللَّهَ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ : «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَعَى النَّجَاشِيَّ فِي الْيَوْمِ الَّذِي مَاتَ فِيهِ، وَخَرَجَ بِهِمْ إِلَى الْمُصَلَّى، فَصَفَّ بِهِمْ، وَكَبَّرَ عَلَيْهِ أَرْبَعَ تَكْبِيرَاتٍ.» (البخاري: باب التكبير على الجنازة أربعا، رقم 1333) وَوَجْهُ (2) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَالصَّلَاةُ أَنْ يُكَبِّرَ تَكْبِيرَةً يَحْمَدُ اللَّهَ قَالَ: رَأَيْتُ الْحَسَنَ «يُصَلِّي عَلَى جِنَازَةِ أَبِي رَجَاءٍ الْعُطَارِدِيِّ عَلَى حِمَارٍ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبه: في الرجل والمرأة يصلي على الجنازة وهو راكب، رقم 11336) وَوَجْهُ (3) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَالصَّلَاةُ أَنْ يُكَبِّرَ تَكْبِيرَةً يَحْمَدُ اللَّهَ أَنَّهُ سَأَلَ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ، كَيْفَ يُصَلَّى عَلَى الْجَنَازَةِ؟ فَقَالَ أَبُو هُرَيْرَةَ: أَنَا، لَعَمْرُ اللَّهِ أُخْبِرُكَ. أَتَّبِعُهَا مِنْ أَهْلِهَا. فَإِذَا وُضِعَتْ كَبَّرْتُ وَحَمِدْتُ اللَّهَ وَصَلَّيْتُ عَلَى نَبِيِّهِ ثُمَّ أَقُولُ: اللَّهُمَّ عَبْدُكَ، وَابْنُ عَبْدِكَ، وَابْنُ أَمَتِكَ. كَانَ يَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا أَنْتَ وَأَنَّ مُحَمَّداً عَبْدُكَ وَرَسُولُكَ. وَأَنْتَ أَعْلَمُ بِهِ اللَّهُمَّ إِنْ كَانَ مُحْسِنًا فَرِدَّ فِي إِحْسَانِهِ. وَإِنْ كَانَ مُسِيئاً فَتَجَاوَزْ عَنْ سَيِّئَاتِهِ. اللَّهُمَّ لَا تَحْرِمْنَا أَجْرَهُ وَلَا تَفْتِنَا بَعْدَهُ (موطأ مالك: ما يقول المصلي على الجنازة، رقم 775) أُصُولُ: نماز جنازہ کی پہلی تکبیر میں ثناء، دوسری میں درود، تیسری میں میت کے لئے دعاء، اور چوتھی میں سلام پھیر دیا جائے، بس یہ مکمل نماز جنازہ ہے. ثُمَّ يُكَبِّرُ تَكْبِيرَةً ثَالِثَةً يَدْعُو فِيهَا لِنَفْسِهِ وَلِلْمَيِّتِ وَلِلْمُسْلِمِينَ ثُمَّ يُكَبِّرُ تَكْبِيرَةً رَابِعَةً وَيُسَلِّمُ وَلَا يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ إِلَّا فِي التَّكْبِيرَةِ الْأُولَى. وَلَا يُصَلَّى عَلَى مَيِّتٍ فِي مَسْجِدِ جَمَاعَةٍ كَـ فَإِذَا حَمَلُوهُ عَلَى سَرِيرِهِ أَخَذُوا بِقَوَائِمِهِ وَيَمْشُونَ بِهِ مُسْرِعِينَ دُونَ الْخَبَبِ. وَجْهُ (1) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَالصَّلَاةُ أَنْ يُكَبِّرَ تَكْبِيرَةً يَحْمَدُ اللَّهَ \ عَنْ طَلْحَةَ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَوْفٍ قَالَ: «صَلَّيْتُ خَلْفَ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما عَلَى جِنَازَةٍ، فَقَرَأَ بِفَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ قَالَ: لِيَعْلَمُوا أَنَّهَا سُنَّةٌ» (البخاري: باب قراءة فاتحة الكتاب على الجنازة، رقم 1335) وَوَجْهُ (2) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالصَّلَاةُ أَنْ يُكَبِّرَ تَكْبِيرَةً يَحْمَدُ اللَّهَ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: صَلَّى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَلَى جِنَازَةٍ، فَقَالَ: «اللَّهُمَّ اغْفِرْ لِحَيِّنَا وَمَيِّتِنَا وَصَغِيرِنَا وَكَبِيرِنَا وَذَكَرِنَا وَأُنْثَانَا وَشَاهِدِنَا وَغَائِبِنَا، اللَّهُمَّ مَنْ أَحْيَيْتَهُ مِنَّا فَأَحْيِهِ عَلَى الْإِيمَانِ، وَمَنْ تَوَفَّيْتَهُ مِنَّا فَتَوَفَّهُ عَلَى الْإِسْلَامِ، اللَّهُمَّ لَا تَحْرِمْنَا أَجْرَهُ وَلَا تُضِلَّنَا بَعْدَهُ» (سنن أبي داود: باب الدعاء للميت، رقم 3201) وَوَجْهُ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يُصَلَّى عَلَى مَيِّتٍ فِي مَسْجِدِ جَمَاعَةٍ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ صَلَّى عَلَى جَنَازَةٍ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ» (سنن أبي داود: باب الصلاة على الجنازة في المسجد، رقم 3191، والسنن الكبرى للبيهقي: باب الصلاة على الجنازة في المسجد، رقم 7040) وَوَجْهُ (1) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيَّةِ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يُصَلَّى عَلَى مَيِّتٍ فِي مَسْجِدِ جَمَاعَةٍ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّهَا لَمَّا تُوُفِّيَ سَعْدُ بْنُ أَبِي وَقَّاصٍ ... بَلَغَهُنَّ أَنَّ النَّاسَ عَابُوا ذَلِكَ وَقَالُوا مَا كَانَتِ الْجَنَائِزُ يُدْخَلُ بِهَا الْمَسْجِدَ، فَبَلَغَ ذَلِكَ عَائِشَةَ فَقَالَتْ: مَا أَسْرَعَ النَّاسَ إِلَى أَنْ يَعِيبُوا مَا لَا عِلْمَ لَهُمْ بِهِ، عَابُوا عَلَيْنَا أَنْ يُمَرَّ بِجَنَازَةٍ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ، وَمَا صَلَّى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَلَى سُهَيْلِ ابْنِ بَيْضَاءَ إِلَّا فِي جَوْفِ الْمَسْجِدِ (مسلم: باب الصلاة على الجنازة في المسجد، رقم 973) وَوَجْهُ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِذَا حَمَلُوهُ عَلَى سَرِيرِهِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «أَسْرِعُوا بِالْجِنَازَةِ، فَإِنْ تَكُ صَالِحَةً فَخَيْرٌ تُقَدِّمُونَهَا، وَإِنْ يَكُ سِوَى ذَلِكَ فَشَرٌّ تَضَعُونَهُ» أُصُولُ: مسجد میں نماز جنازہ ادا کرنا مکروہ ہے کیوں کہ رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے مسجد میں نماز جنازہ منع فرمایا ہے.
Regarding the prayer over the deceased. The prayer is that he says the first takbir, praising Allah the Exalted after it, then he says a second takbir and sends blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) ... and upon her was a green bier, so he stood at her waist, and prayed over her like his prayer over a man, then he sat. Al-Ala ibn Ziyad said: O Abu Hamzah, was the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) praying over the funeral like your prayer? He says four takbirs and stands at the head of a man and the waist of a woman? He said: Yes. (Sunan Abi Dawud) ... Proof (3) the hadith for establishing: 'If he is buried and not prayed over, prayer is offered at his grave' ... We narrated from Samurah ibn Jundub: I prayed behind the Prophet (peace be upon him) over a woman who died in childbirth, and he stood at her middle. (Bukhari, Muslim, Abi Dawud) ... Proof (1) the hadith for establishing the prayer: 'He says a takbir praising Allah' from Abu Hurairah: that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) announced the death of an-Najashi on the day he died, and went out with them to the prayer ground, formed them in rows, and said four takbirs over him. (Bukhari) ... Proof (2) the saying of the Tabi'i for establishing the prayer: 'He says a takbir praising Allah' said: I saw al-Hasan praying over the funeral of Abu Raja' al-Utaridi while riding a donkey. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) ... Proof (3) the saying of the Companion for establishing the prayer: 'He says a takbir praising Allah' that he asked Abu Hurairah, how is prayer said over the deceased? So Abu Hurairah said: I, by the life of Allah, will inform you. I follow it from its people. When it is placed, I say takbir, praise Allah, and send blessings upon His Prophet, then I say: O Allah, Your servant, son of Your servant, son of Your maidservant. He used to bear witness that there is no god but You and that Muhammad is Your servant and Your Messenger. You know him best. O Allah, if he was righteous, increase him in goodness, and if he was evil, overlook his sins. O Allah, do not deprive us of his reward and do not lead us astray after him. (Muwatta Malik) ... Principle: In the first takbir of janazah prayer, praise; in the second, salawat; in the third, du'a for the deceased; and in the fourth, taslim. This complete janazah prayer. Then he says a third takbir, making du'a in it for himself, the deceased, and the Muslims; then he says a fourth takbir and says taslim, and he does not raise his hands except in the first takbir. And prayer is not offered over a deceased in a mosque in congregation, as when they carry him on his bier, they take its legs and walk with him briskly without jogging. Proof (1) the Shafi'i evidence: the saying of the Companion for establishing the prayer: 'He says a takbir praising Allah' from Talhah ibn Abdullah ibn Awf: I prayed behind Ibn Abbas over a funeral, and he recited the Opening of the Book and said: So that they know it is a sunnah. (Bukhari) ... Proof (2) the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith for establishing the prayer: 'He says a takbir praising Allah' from Abu Hurairah: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed over a funeral and said: 'O Allah, forgive our living and our dead, our young and our old, our male and our female, our present and our absent. O Allah, whom You keep alive among us, keep him alive in faith; whom You take among us, take him in Islam. O Allah, do not deprive us of his reward and do not lead us astray after him.' (Abi Dawud) ... Proof (1) the hadith for establishing that prayer is not offered over a deceased in a mosque as a congregation: from Abu Hurairah, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever prays over a deceased in the mosque, nothing is upon him.' (Abi Dawud, Baihaqi) ... Proof (1) the Shafi'i evidence: the saying of the Companion for establishing that prayer is not offered over a deceased in a mosque as a congregation: from Aisha: when Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas died... it reached her that people criticized that, saying that funerals used not to be brought into the mosque. That reached Aisha and she said: 'How quickly people criticize what they have no knowledge of! They criticized us for passing a funeral in the mosque; the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not pray over Suhayl ibn Bayda except in the middle of the mosque.' (Muslim) ... Proof (1) the hadith for establishing: 'When they carry him on his bier' from Abu Hurairah from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Hasten with the funeral; if it is a righteous soul, then it is good you are sending forward; if it is other than that, then it is evil you are putting down.' Principle: Praying janazah in the mosque is makruh because the Messenger (peace be upon him) forbade praying janazah in the mosque.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the Quduri matn on janazah prayer. It combines the core ruling with multiple proofs and addresses a dispute with the Shafi'i school. The passage opens by stating the ruling: janazah prayer consists of four takbirs. In the first takbir, one praises Allah; in the second, sends blessings on the Prophet; in the third, supplicates for oneself, the deceased, and all Muslims; in the fourth, says the taslim. Hands are raised only in the first takbir. The text then cites several proofs: a hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub about the imam standing at the middle of a woman's body, a hadith from Abu Hurairah regarding four takbirs over an-Najashi, the practice of the tabi'i al-Hasan, and the explicit instruction of Abu Hurairah on the supplication. Following the description, the matn adds two additional rulings: it is not permissible to pray over a deceased inside a mosque in congregation, and the bier should be carried briskly by its legs without running. The commentary then presents evidence for the Shafi'i position regarding recitation of al-Fatihah and the permissibility of praying in the mosque, quoting Ibn Abbas and Aisha. The Hanafi position is that praying janazah in a mosque is makruh tanzihi, based on the general prohibition of the Prophet. The ruling on carrying the bier is supported by the hadith urging haste. Throughout, the passage maintains the Hanafi stance while acknowledging the opposing evidence.

Key Terms
تَكْبِيرَة (takbīrah): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' in janazah prayer; there are four takbirs total.
تَسْلِيم (taslīm): The concluding salutation of the prayer, said after the fourth takbir in janazah.
مَكْرُوه (makrūh): Disliked; an act that is not sinful but should be avoided. In this context, praying janazah in the mosque is makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, how many takbirs are there in janazah prayer, and when are hands raised?
A) Four takbirs, hands raised in all of them.
B) Five takbirs, hands raised in the first only.
C) Four takbirs, hands raised in the first only.
D) Three takbirs, hands raised in the first two.

Key Takeaway
Janazah prayer consists of four takbirs with specific supplications, and it is makruh tanzihi to pray it inside a mosque.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Hanafi Rulings on the Funeral Prayer and Burial Practices
Rulings with proofs for funeral prayer, carrying, and burial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for the funeral prayer (number of takbirs, raising hands, prohibition of congregational prayer in the mosque) and burial (carrying, walking pace, grave type) and identify the supporting hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Four takbirs, hands raised only in the first, no congregational janaza in mosques, and lahd burial – all based on Sunnah and Companions' practice.

This lesson examines the Hanafi positions on the funeral prayer and burial as presented in Al-Quduri's matn, supported by ahadith from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud. You will learn the precise structure of the prayer, the rationale behind prohibiting janaza in the mosque, and the sunnah way of carrying the bier and digging the grave. Understanding these details ensures your practice aligns with the Hanafi school's evidence-based methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List the main topics: the funeral prayer (takbirs, raising hands, supplications), prohibition of mosque congregation, carrying the bier, walking speed, and grave digging. For each, note the specific Hanafi ruling stated in the matn.
The matn uses imperative and negative forms to indicate rulings: e.g., 'لا يرفع يديه إلا في التكبيرة الأولى' indicates prohibition of raising hands except first takbir.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
For each ruling, find the hadith or companion statement cited in the text. Note the reference (e.g., Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). Distinguish between a hadith (marfu') and a companion saying (mawquf).
The text uses 'وجه الحديث' or 'وجه قول الصحابي' to introduce proofs.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each dalil proves the Hanafi ruling. For example, the hadith 'أسْرِعُوا بالجنازة' (hasten with the funeral) is used to justify walking quickly but not trotting, as 'دون الخبب' is also specified in another hadith.
Pay attention to how the Hanafi school interprets general commands and companion actions.
4
Examine the inter-madhhab dispute on janaza in mosque
Contrast the Hanafi ruling (makruh tahrimi) with the Shafi'i position (permissible). Identify the Shafi'i proof (hadith of Suhayl ibn Bayda in Muslim) and the Hanafi response (interpretation as exception or limited to individual prayer).
This dispute is a classic example of ikhtilaf based on different prioritization of evidence.
5
Synthesize the burial adab
Combine the rulings on carrying (all four sides, starting with right), walking pace (quick but not trotting), not sitting until bier placed, and grave digging (lahd preferred, shaqq as alternative; entering from qibla side).
The Urdu note at the end summarizes the two grave types: lahd (sunnah) and shaqq (permissible if needed).

لِي خَدًّا وَانْصِبُوا عَلَيَّ اللَّبِنَ نَصْبًا كَمَا صُنِعَ بِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ (مسلم) وَجْهٌ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيُحْفَرُ الْقَبْرُ وَيُلْحَدُ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ اللَّحْدُ لَنَا وَالشَّقُّ لِغَيْرِنَا (مسلم) وَجْهٌ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيُدْخَلُ الْمَيِّتُ مِمَّا يَلِي الْقِبْلَةَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ دَخَلَ قَبْرًا لَيْلًا فَأَسْرَجَ لَهُ سِرَاجٌ فَأَخَذَهُ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْقِبْلَةِ وَقَالَ رَحِمَكَ اللَّهُ إِنْ كُنْتَ لَأَوَّاهًا تَلَّاءً (رواه) أُصُولٌ قَبْرٍ كَهُونْ كَا دو طَرِيقَ هَيْنْ 1 لَحْدَ يَعْنِي بَغْلِي قَبْرَ أَوْر يَهِي مَسْنُونٌ طَرِيقَةً هَيْنْ 2 شَقَّ يَعْنِي قَبْرَ كُو سِيدَّا كَهْودَجَائِزٌ هَيْ جَبْكِه مِتِّى نَرْمُ هُوا وَقَبْرَ بَيْتْ جَانَى كَا أَنْدِيشَهُ هُوا
Regarding the prayer over the deceased: Then he says the third takbir and in it supplicates for himself, for the deceased, and for the Muslims. Then he says the fourth takbir and makes the salutation. And he does not raise his hands except in the first takbir. And the funeral prayer is not performed over a deceased in a mosque congregation. When they carry him on his bier, they take hold of its legs and walk with him quickly without a trot. And the prayer is to say a takbir praising Allah. From Talhah ibn Abdullah ibn Awf: I prayed behind Ibn Abbas over a funeral, and he recited Fatihah, saying 'So that they know it is Sunnah' (Bukhari). And the prayer is to say a takbir praising Allah. From Abu Hurayrah: The Messenger of Allah prayed over a funeral and said: 'O Allah, forgive our living and our dead, our young and our old, our males and our females, our present and our absent; O Allah, whom You give life among us, let him live on faith, and whom You cause to die among us, let him die on Islam; O Allah, do not deprive us of his reward, and do not lead us astray after him' (Abu Dawud). Direction: The hadith proves the ruling 'And the funeral prayer is not performed over a deceased in a mosque congregation' from Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet said: 'Whoever prays over a funeral in the mosque, there is nothing upon him' (Abu Dawud). Proof: The Shafi'i's evidence from the statement of the female companion to prove the prohibition: From Aishah that when Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas died... (Muslim). Direction: The hadith for proving the ruling 'When they carry him on his bier' from Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet: 'Hurry with the funeral; if it is righteous, it is good you are sending ahead, and if otherwise, it is evil you are putting off your necks' (Bukhari). Direction: The hadith for proving from Ibn Mas'ud: 'We asked our Prophet about walking with the funeral, and he said: Less than a trot' (Abu Dawud). Direction: The companion's statement for proof: Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: 'Whoever follows a funeral should carry all sides of the bier, for that is from the Sunnah; then if he wishes he may volunteer, and if he wishes he may leave' (Abu Dawud). Direction: The companion's statement: 'I saw Ibn Umar at a funeral; they carried the four sides of the bier, starting with the right, then he moved away from it...' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). Direction: The companion's statement for proof of the ruling 'When they reach his grave, it is disliked for people to sit': from Abu Hurayrah that he would not sit until the bier was placed (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). Direction: The companion's statement for proof of the ruling 'And the grave is dug as a side-chamber': that Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas said in his illness in which he died: 'Dig for me a niche and set up bricks over me standing, as was done with the Messenger of Allah' (Muslim). Direction: The hadith for proof: from Ibn Abbas, the Prophet said: 'Side-chamber (lahd) is for us, and the trench (shaqq) is for others' (Muslim). Direction: The hadith for proof of 'And the deceased is entered from the direction of the qibla': from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet entered a grave at night, a lamp was lit for him, and he took him from the direction of the qibla and said: 'May Allah have mercy on you; you were indeed one who sighed much and recited the Quran' (narrated). Principles: There are two ways of digging a grave: 1) Lahd, meaning side-chamber, and this is the sunnah method. 2) Shaqq, meaning digging the grave straight down; this is also permissible when the soil is soft and there is fear of the grave collapsing.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri with its proofs is a comprehensive summary of key Hanafi rulings in funeral rites. The passage type is a ruling with proof, combining the matn of the author with extensive hadith and companion evidence. The matn first details the structure of the funeral prayer: after the first takbir (with raising hands), the second takbir (not detailed here), then the third takbir for supplication for oneself, the deceased, and all Muslims, then the fourth takbir, and finally the salutation (taslim). The Hanafi position is that hands are raised only for the first takbir; this is based on the practice of the Companions and is a distinctive feature of the school. Next, the matn states that the funeral prayer is not performed in a mosque congregation. This is a Hanafi ruling: it is makruh tahrimi to hold congregational janaza prayer inside a mosque. The Shafi'i school allows it, citing the hadith of Aishah that the Prophet prayed over Suhayl ibn Bayda inside the mosque. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition is based on other evidence, and the hadith cited by Shafi'i is interpreted as an exception or as referring to an individual prayer, not a congregation. The text then covers carrying the bier: bearers should take hold of the legs of the bier and walk quickly but not at a trot (khabab). The proof from Ibn Mas'ud shows that the sunnah is to carry all four sides of the bier, starting with the right side. When the funeral reaches the grave, it is disliked (makruh) for people to sit before the bier is placed down. The grave should be dug as a side-chamber (lahd), which is the sunnah; the trench (shaqq) is permissible only if necessary (e.g., soft soil). The deceased is entered into the grave from the direction of the qibla. These rulings are all grounded in the practice of the Prophet and the Companions, as transmitted in the hadith and آثار cited. The Urdu note at the end summarizes the two methods of grave digging.

Key Terms
التكبيرة (takbirah): Each 'Allahu Akbar' uttered in the funeral prayer; the Hanafi school uses four takbirs.
اللحد (lahd): A side-chamber dug into the wall of the grave to place the deceased, protecting from soil.
الشق (shaqq): A straight trench grave, used when soil is soft or lahd is not possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in Al-Quduri, why is it considered makruh tahrimi to perform the funeral prayer in a mosque congregation?
A) Because the mosque is only for the five daily prayers.
B) Because the Prophet never did it in congregation, and the practice of the Companions supports this.
C) Because the hadith states that the prayer is invalid if done in the mosque.
D) Because it is a sin to enter a mosque with a janaza.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes four takbirs with hands raised only in the first, prohibits congregational janaza in mosques (makruh tahrimi), and recommends lahd burial with specific carrying and walking etiquette.

Salah — Prayer
