Prayer Inside, Around, and on Top of the Kaaba
Ruling on prayer inside and atop the Kaaba with hadith evidence and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer inside and on the roof of the Kaaba, and explain the evidence and the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
Prayer inside the Kaaba is valid for both fard and nafl; the roof is permissible but disliked.

This lesson from Al-Quduri addresses a unique scenario: praying inside the sacred Kaaba itself. The Hanafi school affirms its validity based on prophetic practice, while acknowledging a scholarly difference with Imam al-Shafi'i. Understanding this ruling reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes prophetic action (fi'l) over purely spatial logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary rulings
State the Hanafi position on prayer inside the Kaaba and on its roof, including the level of validity and any dislike.
The text explicitly says prayer inside is jai'z, and on the roof is jai'z but makruh.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the hadith of Ibn Umar and identify what it proves about the Prophet's action inside the Kaaba.
The Prophet prayed between the two front pillars – this is the proof for permissibility.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection
Understand why Imam al-Shafi'i considers prayer inside invalid when facing the open door, based on the requirement to face the qibla directly.
For Shafi'i, the open door breaks the orientation to the Kaaba itself.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
See how Hanafis reconcile the hadith with the principle of facing the qibla – the interior of the Kaaba is itself qibla.
The Prophet's action is the strongest proof, and facing any direction inside suffices.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf – the real-world difference between the two schools for a person praying inside the Kaaba.
Hanafis pray without restriction; Shafi'is avoid facing the open door.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ فِي الْكَعْبَةِ
الصَّلاةُ فِي الْكَعْبَةِ جَائِزَةٌ فَرْضُهَا وَنَفْلُهَا فَإِنْ صَلَّى الإِمَامُ بِجَمَاعَةٍ فَجَعَلَ بَعْضُهُمْ ظَهْرَهُ إِلَى ظَهْرِ الْإِمَامِ جَازَ إِلَى آخِرِهِ وَإِذَا صَلَّى الْإِمَامُ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ تَخَلَّفَ النَّاسُ حَوْلَ الْكَعْبَةِ إِلَخَ فَمَنْ كَانَ مِنْهُمْ أَقْرَبَ إلَى الْكَعْبَةِ مِنْ الْإِمَامِ جَازَتْ صَلَاتُهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي جَانِبِ الْإِمَامِ وَمَنْ صَلَّى عَلَى ظَهْرِ الْكَعْبَةِ جَازَتْ صَلَاتُهُ
وَجْه: (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ قُتِلَ مِنْ الْبُغَاةِ أَوْ قُطَّاعِ الطَّرِيقِ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: «دَخَلَ النَّبِيُّ الْبَيْتَ وَأُسَامَةُ بْنُ زَيْدٍ، وَعُثْمَانُ بْنُ طَلْحَةَ، وَبِلَالٌ، فَأَطَالَ ثُمَّ خَرَجَ كُنْتُ أَوَّلَ النَّاسِ دَخَلَ عَلَى أَثَرِهِ، فَسَأَلْتُ بِلَالًا : أَيْنَ صَلَّى؟ قَالَ : بَيْنَ الْعَمُودَيْنِ الْمُقَدَّمَيْنِ» (بخاري شريف: باب الصلاة بين السواري في غير جماعة،نمبر504 مسلم شریف: باب استحباب دخول الكعبة للحاج وغيره والصلاة فيها والدعاء في نواحيها كلها، نمبر 1329)
وَجْه : (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ صَلَّى عَلَى ظَهْرِ الْكَعْبَةِ جَازَتْ صَلَاتُهُ عَنْ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى أَنْ يُصَلَّى فِي سَبْعَةِ مَوَاطِنَ: فِي المَرْبَلَةِ، وَالمَجْزَرَةِ، وَالمَقْبَرَةِ، وَقَارِعَةِ الطَّرِيقِ، وَفِي الحَمَّامِ، وَفِي مَعَاطِنِ الإِبِلِ ، وَفَوْقَ ظَهْرِ بَيْتِ اللَّهِ " (سنن ترمذي : باب ما جاء في كراهية ما يصلى إليه وفيه، نمبر 346 سنن ابن ماجه بَابُ الْمَوَاضِعِ الَّتِي تُكْرَهُ فِيهَا الصَّلَاةُ، نمبر 746)
اصول: خانہ کعبہ کے باہر چاروں طرف نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے، نیز احناف کے نزدیک جوفِ کعبہ میں بھی نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے، البتہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جوف کعبہ میں دروازہ کی جانب ( جبکہ دروازہ کھلا ہوا ہو) رخ کر کے نماز جائز نہیں۔
اصول : خانہ کعبہ کے باہر جماعت سے نماز ہو رہی ہے تو جس شخص کی پیٹھ امام کی طرف ہو ، اس کی نماز نہیں ہو گی، باقی سب کی ہو جائے گی۔
اصول: خانہ کعبہ کی چھت پر نماز جائز ہے البتہ مکروہ ہے۔
Chapter of Prayer in the Kaaba. Prayer in the Kaaba is permissible, its obligatory and supererogatory. If the imam prays with a congregation, and some of them make their backs to the back of the imam, it is permissible to the end of it. And when the imam prays in the Sacred Mosque, the people remain around the Kaaba, etc. So whoever among them is closer to the Kaaba than the imam, his prayer is permissible if he is not on the side of the imam. And whoever prays on the roof of the Kaaba, his prayer is permissible. Evidence (1): Hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The Prophet entered the House with Usama, Uthman ibn Talha and Bilal, and stayed long. Then he came out, and I was the first to enter after him. I asked Bilal: Where did he pray? He said: Between the two front pillars.' Evidence (1) for the permissibility of praying on the roof of the Kaaba: From Ibn Umar that the Prophet forbade praying in seven places: the garbage dump, the slaughterhouse, the graveyard, the middle of the road, the bathroom, the resting places of camels, and on top of the House of Allah. Principle: It is permissible to pray on all four sides of the Kaaba, and according to the Hanafis, prayer inside the Kaaba is also permissible. However, Imam Shafi'i says that inside the Kaaba, facing the door (when the door is open) is not permissible. Principle: If prayer is being performed in congregation outside the Kaaba, the prayer of the person whose back is towards the imam is not valid, but the rest are valid. Principle: Prayer on the roof of the Kaaba is permissible but disliked.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri covers the rulings on prayer in relation to the Kaaba. It begins with a ruling statement: prayer inside the Kaaba is valid for both obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers. The text then addresses a congregation scenario: if the imam prays inside the Kaaba and some people pray outside with their backs towards the imam's back, their prayer is valid (provided they are within the line of the imam's direction). However, if someone prays outside while the imam is inside the Sacred Mosque, and that person is closer to the Kaaba than the imam, their prayer is valid only if they are not on the same side as the imam (i.e., they must not be directly behind the imam in a straight line). Next, the ruling on praying on the roof of the Kaaba: it is permissible (jai'z) but disliked (makruh), as noted in the Urdu principle. The passage then provides hadith evidence: the first hadith (Bukhari and Muslim) shows that the Prophet prayed inside the Kaaba between two pillars, proving permissibility. The second hadith (Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah) lists seven places where prayer is forbidden, including 'on top of the House of Allah,' which seems to contradict the ruling. However, the Hanafi school interprets the prohibition as indicating karahah (dislike) rather than tahrim (unlawfulness), reconciling the hadith with the permissibility. Finally, the passage includes an inter-madhhab dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if one prays inside the Kaaba facing the open door, the prayer is invalid, because one would be facing outward from the Kaaba, whereas the Hanafi position allows it in all directions. The Tarjih (preferred view) in the Hanafi school is the permissibility of praying inside the Kaaba in any direction.

Key Terms
الكعبة (al-Ka'bah): The sacred house of Allah in Mecca, the qibla for Muslims.
ظهر الكعبة (zahr al-Ka'bah): The roof of the Kaaba. The text rules on praying on top of it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a person praying fard salah on the roof of the Kaaba?
A) Valid and recommended.
B) Valid but disliked.
C) Invalid and must be repeated.
D) Only valid if it's nafl.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that prayer inside the Kaaba is valid in any direction based on prophetic practice, and prayer on the roof is valid but disliked.

Nullification of I'tikaf: Intercourse and Exit Without Excuse
Ruling on nullification by intercourse and exit without excuse (intra-Hanafi dispute)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nullification of i'tikaf by intercourse and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on exit without excuse, identifying the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Intercourse nullifies i'tikaf absolutely; leaving the mosque even for an hour invalidates it according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn require more than half a day.

This passage from al-Quduri presents two rulings on nullification of i'tikaf. The first is absolute: intercourse, whether intentional or forgetful, nullifies i'tikaf. The second reveals a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: does a short exit without excuse break the seclusion? Abu Hanifa holds that any intentional exit nullifies, while his two disciples restrict nullification to exits exceeding half a day. This lesson will help you parse the positions and understand the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two nullifying acts
The passage lists two acts that nullify i'tikaf: intercourse (first sentence) and exit without excuse (second sentence). Note that the first is agreed upon, the second is disputed.
The first ruling covers all cases of intercourse, intentional or forgetful.
2
Extract the three positions on exit
For exit without excuse, three positions emerge: Abu Hanifa says any duration nullifies; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say only if longer than half a day.
The Sahibayn require a clear threshold to indicate abandonment of seclusion.
3
Locate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a mu'takif who steps out for a few minutes would have to restart i'tikaf per Abu Hanifa but not per the Sahibayn, unless gone many hours.
This affects real scenarios like visiting family or taking a short break.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah) adopted Abu Hanifa's stricter view as the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The stronger evidence from the sunna supports this tarjih.
5
Note the underlying usul
The dispute reflects a difference in interpreting the sunna: Abu Hanifa gives the prohibition its literal generality; the Sahibayn apply qiyas to permit short exits, similar to negligible acts like eating.
Understanding this usul difference clarifies why the positions diverge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ جَامَعَ الْمُعْتَكِفُ لَيْلًا أَوْ نَهَارًا عَامِدًا أَوْ نَاسِيًا بَطَلَ اعْتِكَافُهُ وَلَوْ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ سَاعَةً بِغَيْرِ عُذْرٍ فَسَدَ اعْتِكَافُهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَا يَفْسُدُ حَتَّى يَكُونَ أَكْثَرُ مِنْ نِصْفِ يَوْمٍ.
If the mu'takif has intercourse by night or day, intentionally or forgetfully, his i'tikaf is nullified. And if he leaves the mosque for an hour without an excuse, his i'tikaf is invalidated according to Abu Hanifa. But Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said it is not invalidated until it exceeds half a day.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings. First, intercourse during i'tikaf, whether at night or day, deliberate or forgetful, invalidates the i'tikaf completely (batala). Second, leaving the mosque without a valid excuse (like the call of nature or Friday) triggers a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Sahibayn). Abu Hanifa holds that even a short exit (one hour) nullifies the i'tikaf, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that it only nullifies if the exit exceeds half a day. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa, as stated in al-Hidayah and other works.

Key Terms
جَامَعَ (jama'a): Had sexual intercourse
عَامِدًا أَوْ نَاسِيًا ('amidan aw nasiyan): Intentionally or forgetfully
نِصْفِ يَوْم (nisfi yawm): Half a day

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, how long must a mu'takif be outside the mosque without excuse for the i'tikaf to become invalid?
A) Any amount of time
B) More than half a day
C) More than an hour
D) More than a day

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, i'tikaf is nullified by intercourse absolutely, and by exit without excuse according to the mufta bihi view of Abu Hanifa.

Ruling on Muhrim Killing Game When Compelled
Ruling on a muhrim compelled to eat game, killing it, and the required compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a muhrim kills game under compulsion and identify the Quranic proof that necessitates compensation.

Core Idea
Even compulsion does not remove the penalty for killing game in ihram.

This passage presents a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: necessity does not nullify the obligation of compensation (jaza') for a muhrim who kills game. The proof is drawn from the Quranic verse on fidyah, showing that compulsion is recognized but the penalty remains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The case involves a muhrim who is compelled to eat game meat and kills the game himself.
Compulsion means a genuine necessity, such as fear of starvation.
2
State the hukm
The ruling is that compensation (jaza') is wajib upon him.
The text says 'فَعَلَيْهِ الْجَزَاءُ' — upon him is the compensation.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 2:196, which commands a ransom (fidyah) for a muhrim with a valid excuse. The Hanafi school draws an analogy: just as fidyah is required for shaving the head due to illness, compensation is required for killing game under compulsion.
The verse is cited directly in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ اضْطَرَّ الْمُحْرِمُ إِلَى أَكْلِ لَم صَيْدٍ فَقَتَلَهُ فَعَلَيْهِ الجَزَاء ١٥ وَجْهٌ : (۱) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِنْ اضْطَرَّ الْمُحْرِمُ إِلَى أَكْلِ لَحْمِ صَيْدِ ﴿فَمَن كَانَ مِنكُم مَّرِيضًا أَوْ بِهِ أَذًى مِّن رَّأْسِهِ فَفِدْيَةٌ مِّن صِيَامٍ أَوْ صَدَقَةٍ أَوْ نُسُكٍ﴾ (سورة البقرة، 2:196)
If the muhrim is compelled to eat meat of game and he kills it, then upon him is the compensation. Proof: The verse for the establishment of: if the muhrim is compelled to eat meat of game ... then a ransom of fasting or charity or sacrifice.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage states a ruling and its proof. The ruling: if a person in the state of ihram is forced by necessity to eat game meat, and he himself kills the game, then he must pay compensation (jaza). The proof is the Quranic verse (2:196) which prescribes a ransom for a muhrim who has a valid excuse. The Hanafi position is that the compensation is determined by the value of the game or equivalent sacrifice.

Key Terms
الْجَزَاء (al-jaza'): Compensation due for killing game while in ihram; it can be a sacrifice, feeding the poor, or value.
الْمُحْرِم (al-muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when a muhrim is compelled to eat game and kills it?
A) It is permissible without any penalty.
B) He must pay compensation (jaza').
C) It is forbidden and he must repent.
D) He must fast for three days.

Key Takeaway
Compensation for killing game in ihram is wajib even when compelled.
